title": "Achiote paste",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Achiote paste, Barbecue recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#achiotepaste #garlic #vegetables #mexicanoregano #spices #spice #annattoseeds #achiote #pestleandmortar #pork #cinnamon \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Achiote paste or Recado rojo or is a popular blend of spices from Mexico used to season meat or vegetables\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 156\n|PortionCalories = 39\n|DatePublished=25th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Tofu marinading in achiote paste\n |Servings = Servings: 4 - Makes 1 cup of [[Achiote|achiote]] paste\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 10 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Tofu marinading in achiote paste.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Even tofu tastes good in this</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.2</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Great vegetarian dish</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''[[Achiote]] paste''' or '''Recado rojo''' or  is a popular blend of [[Spices|spices]] from Mexico used to season [[Meat|meat]] or [[Vegetables|vegetables]]. Originally a Mayan blend, it is now strongly associated with the [[Mexican Cuisine|Mexican cuisine]] of Yucatan.\n\nThe [[Spice|spice]] mixture usually includes [[Annatto|annatto]], [[Mexican oregano]], [[Cumin|cumin]], [[Clove|clove]], [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]], [[Black pepper|black pepper]], [[Allspice|allspice]], [[Garlic|garlic]], and [[Salt|salt]]. The [[Annatto seeds|annatto seeds]] dye the mixture red, and this gives the [[Meat|meat]] or [[Vegetables|vegetables]] it seasons a distinctive red hue.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| &#188; cup [[annatto seeds]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Mexican oregano]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Black peppercorns|black peppercorns]]\n| 2 whole [[Cloves|cloves]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 5 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled\n| &#189; cup [[Bitter orange|bitter orange]] [[Juice|juice]] or 1/3 cup [[White wine vinegar|white wine vinegar]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Using a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]] or a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]], grind the dry [[Spices|spices]]\n| Peel and crush the [[Garlic|garlic]], mix with the [[Salt|salt]], [[Ground|ground]] [[Spice|spice]] mix and [[Orange juice|orange juice]] and mix to a smooth paste.\n| Rub the mixture onto [[Chicken|chicken]], [[Pork|pork]] or [[Fish|fish]] and [[Marinate|marinate]] in a cool place for 4-6 hours then cook as you would normally.\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#achiotepaste #garlic #vegetables #mexicanoregano #spices #spice #annattoseeds #achiote #pestleandmortar #pork #cinnamon </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

Originally a Mayan blend, it is now strongly associated with the [[Mexican Cuisine]] of Yucatan.\n\nThe [[Spice|spice]] mixture usually includes [[Annatto|annatto]], [[Mexican oregano]], [[Cumin|cumin]], [[Clove|clove]], [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]], [[Black pepper|black pepper]], [[Allspice|allspice]], [[Garlic|garlic]], and [[Salt|salt]]. title": "Anticuchos de corazon",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Anticuchos de corazon recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#heart #anticuchosdecorazon #garlic #cumin #marinade #beef #redpepper #greenpepper #unusualrecipes #marinated #capsicum \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Anticuchos are popular and inexpensive dishes that originated in Peru, and popular also in other Andean states consisting of small pieces of grilled\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 401\n|PortionCalories = 80\n|DatePublished=26th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = 5\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 10 hours, 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 hours, 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Anticuchos de corazon recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Super street food</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This was nice and hearty \ud83d\ude02 </span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nAnticuchos are popular and inexpensive dishes that originated in Peru, and popular also in other Andean states consisting of small pieces of [[Grilled|grilled]] skewered [[Meat|meat]].\n\nAnticuchos can be readily found on streetcarts and street food stalls (anticucheras). The [[Meat|meat]] may be [[Marinated|marinated]] in [[Vinegar|vinegar]] and [[Spices|spices]] (such as [[Cumin|cumin]], aji [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Garlic|garlic]]), and while anticuchos can be made of any type of meat, the most popular are made of [[Beef|beef]] [[Heart|heart]] (anticuchos de corazon). Anticuchos often come with a [[Boiled|boiled]] [[Potato|potato]] on the end of the skewer.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 Beef [[heart]]\n| 2 cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| &frac14; of a cup ground spicy [[red chili]]\n| 2 cups of [[malt vinegar]]\n| 1 teaspoon of ground [[cumin]]\n| 1 teaspoon of achiote ([[annatto]])\n| 1 teaspoon of [[salt]] \n| 1 teaspoon of ground [[black pepper]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place all the above ingredients, other than the [[Heart|heart]], in a bowl and mix thoroughly.\n| Clean the [[Heart|heart]], removing all [[Fat|fat]]. Cut into bite size cubes. Place the heart pieces into the [[Marinade|marinade]] mixture and leave to [[Marinate|marinate]] for about 10 hours or overnight. The heart should be completely covered.\n| After [[Marinating|marinating]], insert [[Meat|meat]] on [[skewers]]. At this stage if desired , some additional ingredients such as [[Green pepper|green pepper]] or [[Red pepper|red pepper]] ([[Capsicum|capsicum]]) or [[Corn|corn]]-on-cob (cut to a similar size to the [[Heart|heart]], may be also inserted on the skewers.)  \n| The skewered [[Heart|heart]] should then be cooked on a [[Barbecue|barbecue]] [[Grill|grill]], turning frequently and brushing with the [[Marinade|marinade]] mix. When they are well done they should be served immediately.\n}}\n===Variations===\nIf [[Heart|heart]] is not to your taste, try a less-authentic version using a good cut of [[Beef|beef]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Offal recipes]]\n[[Category:Peruvian recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#heart #anticuchosdecorazon #garlic #cumin #marinade #beef #redpepper #greenpepper #unusualrecipes #marinated #capsicum </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Argentinian chicken, Main course recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#argentinianchicken #chicken #oliveoil #miseenplace #chickenstock #blend #garlic #sweetpepper #blender #paprika #oregano \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This recipe was recently added by Graciela Narro, one of our Argentinian visitors\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2017\n|PortionCalories = 504\n|DatePublished=17th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 55 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 45 minutes \n |Image = [[Image:Argentinian chicken recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Easy, peasy</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">A nice simple meal - glad I made it.  Thanks Graciela.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis recipe was recently added by [[User:Graciela Narro|Graciela Narro]], one of our Argentinian visitors.  I have converted it to our standard format and after cooking it , clarified some of the quantities and slightly adjusted the cooking times.\n\nThis is a fabulous recipe and so easy to make!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 800g [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces (bone in)\n| A bunch of leaves of [[Parsley|parsley]]\n| [[Garlic]] to taste, peeled.  I used 6 fat cloves of garlic\n| Half a medium size [[Onion|onion]], peeled and roughly chopped\n| 2 teaspoons of dried [[Oregano|oregano]]\n| 1 heaped teaspoon of [[Paprika|paprika]] powder\n| 1 large red [[Sweet pepper|sweet pepper]], deseeded\n| &#188; cup of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 3 tablespoons of [[Vinegar|white wine vinegar]].\n| 2 heaped teaspoons of [[Chicken stock|chicken stock powder]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put the [[Chicken|chicken]] in an [[Oven|oven]] tray\n| Put the rest of the ingredients in the [[Blender|blender]] and blend for 2 minutes\n| Try to check taste\n| Pour it over [[Chicken|chicken]]\n| Cover with a lid or [[tin-foil]] \n| Put it in the top of the [[Oven|oven]] for 45 minutes\n| Check the chicken is properly cooked\n| Enjoy!\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Argentinian chicken ready for the oven.jpg|Poured over the chicken pieces\nImage:Argentinian chicken blending.jpg|The ingredients, ready to [[blend]]\n</gallery>\n===Chef's notes===\nThis recipe is a good candidate for jointing a small [[Chicken|chicken]] - I prefer to also remove the skin in a dish like this, but that's a personal preference.\n\nI added a little extra water after blending as the mix looked rather dry, however this was probably not necessary as the cooked chicken had more than enough sauce. \n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#argentinianchicken #chicken #oliveoil #miseenplace #chickenstock #blend #garlic #sweetpepper #blender #paprika #oregano </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Arroz con pollo",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Arroz con pollo, Chilean recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #rice #arrozconpollo #cilantro #peas #tomatoes #paprika #diced #saffron #oliveoil #onion \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Arroz con pollo (rice with chicken) is a traditional dish that's common throughout Latin America especially in Cuba, Panama, Peru, Puerto Rico, Costa\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4105\n|PortionCalories = 684\n|DatePublished=8th December 2013\n|Author=Carla Cancio-Bello, J.D., on behalf of Cuban Cuisine UK\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 50 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Arroz con pollo recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">So pretty</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">A lovely dish, thanks Carla.  Here's hoping everything is good with you.  Long time no hear???</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\n\nArroz con pollo ([[Rice|rice]] with [[Chicken|chicken]]) is a traditional dish that's common throughout Latin America especially in Cuba, Panama, Peru, Puerto Rico, Costa Rica, and the Dominican Republic. There is a widespread belief among Hispanics in the US that it originated in Puerto Rico but there is no direct evidence for this. However, it resembles [[Paella|paella]], a [[Spanish]] dish, both in its ingredients and cooking technique, and may very well be a New World adaptation of it.\n\nCommon ingredients for arroz con pollo include [[Rice|rice]], [[Vegetables|vegetables]], [[Fresh herbs|fresh herbs]] and [[Chicken|chicken]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.5 kg whole [[Chicken|chicken]] cut into serving pieces - [[Jointing a chicken|see here for step by step details]]\n| [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] to taste\n| [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 4 [[Cloves|cloves]] of fresh, minced [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], chopped\n| 8 oz [[Diced|diced]] [[Red bell pepper|red bell pepper]]\n| 1 can (15 ounce) [[Diced|diced]] [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| &#189; tablespoon sweet [[Paprika|paprika]]\n| &#189; oz chopped [[Cilantro|cilantro]]\n| 6 cups [[Chicken|chicken]] [[Bouillon|bouillon]]\n| a handful of [[Cilantro|cilantro]]\n| 8 [[Saffron|saffron]] threads or 1 teaspoon of food colouring for [[Yellow rice|yellow rice]]\n| 2 cups medium or long-rain [[Rice|rice]]\n| 8 oz canned [[Peas|peas]] (thoroughly drained)\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Season the [[Chicken|chicken]] with two pinches of [[Salt|salt]] and a pinch of [[Pepper|pepper]].\n| Pour enough [[Olive oil|olive oil]] into a large [[Skillet|skillet]] to just barely cover the bottom.\n| Saut\u00e9 [[Chicken|chicken]] in [[Oil|oil]] until [[Brown|brown]]. There are two ways to proceed from here: Either remove the chicken from the [[Skillet|skillet]] or keep it there.\n| Saut\u00e9 [[Garlic|garlic]] until [[Brown|brown]]. Be careful, garlic burns easily.\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]], [[Bell pepper|bell pepper]], [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Paprika|paprika]]. Saut\u00e9 until the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] are tender.\n| Transfer the ingredients to a large [[Stewing|stewing]] pot.\n| Add the [[Cilantro|cilantro]], bouillon and [[Saffron|saffron]] (or food colouring). Bring to a rolling [[Boil|boil]].\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] and mix well. [[Simmer]] over medium heat until the rice is cooked and the liquid is absorbed. Add more [[Broth|broth]] or water if the liquid evaporates before the rice is cooked.\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] to the pot (if you removed it previously) and cover it with [[Rice|rice]]. Wait two to three minutes to allow the chicken to warm.\n| Sprinkle [[Peas|peas]] on top of the [[Rice|rice]]\n}}\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilean recipes]]\n[[Category:Jamaican recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Cuban recipes]]\n\n[[Category:Peruvian recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #rice #arrozconpollo #cilantro #peas #tomatoes #paprika #diced #saffron #oliveoil #onion </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

title": "Arroz tapado",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Arroz tapado, a fruit recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#rice #arroztapado #raisins #lemonjuice #tomatoes #spanish #mincedbeef #garlic #parsley #tomatopaste #panfried \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Arros tapado (Spanish for molded rice) is very popular in Peru and is a favourite among children because the recipe calls for molding\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4054\n|PortionCalories = 675\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 50 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Arroz tapado recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n======Best recipe review======\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">What shape can you make?</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Charlie made a tree last time!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> - [[User:Chef|Jerry]]</span></span>\n}}\n\nArros tapado ([[Spanish]] for molded [[Rice|rice]]) is very popular in Peru and is a favourite among children because the recipe calls for molding rice and [[Minced beef|minced beef]] into a shape.\n\nThe [[Minced beef|minced beef]] preparation is very similar to [[Picadillo|picadillo]] ([[Spanish]] for [[Minced meat|minced meat]]) which is popular throughout Latin America and the Philippines. In most other countries picadillo is served with [[White rice|white rice]] on the side.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 3 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Minced|minced]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 20 ml [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| [[Salt|salt]]\n| 4 cups water\n| 450 g [1 lb] [[Rice|rice]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], finely chopped\n| 900 g [2 lb] of [[Ground beef|ground beef]]\n| 2 [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], finely chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [[Tomato paste|tomato paste]]\n| 4 tablespoons of [[Raisins|raisins]]\n| 5 [[Black olives|black olives]], chopped\n| 3 [[Hard boiled eggs|hard boiled eggs]]; two chopped, one whole\n| 1 tablespoon [[Parsley|parsley]], finely [[Minced|minced]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Saut\u00e9 the [[Garlic|garlic]] in [[Oil|oil]], add a few drops of [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], [[Salt|salt]] and the water and bring to a [[Boil|boil]].\n| Add [[Rice|rice]] and cook until tender. This should take 20 to 25 minutes.\n| In another pan, stir in [[Onions|onions]] and saut\u00e9.\n| Add [[Meat|meat]], [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Tomato paste|tomato paste]], [[Raisins|raisins]], [[Olives|olives]] and cook for 10 minutes, stirring all the while.\n| Gently fold in the chopped [[Egg|egg]] and [[Parsley|parsley]] \n| Take an eight-ounce [[measuring cup]] and coat the inside with a little [[Oil|oil]]. Fill halfway with [[Rice|rice]], add some [[Meat|meat]] filling and add more rice to top of cup. Invert onto a plate and carefully remove cup.\n| Cut the remaining [[Hard-boiled egg|hard-boiled egg]] in half and serve the two halves along side the arroz tapado on the same plate.\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Peruvian recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rice #arroztapado #raisins #lemonjuice #tomatoes #spanish #mincedbeef #garlic #parsley #tomatopaste #panfried </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

See '''Chef's Notes''' below\n| [[Salt]], to taste\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Wash and drain the [[Rice|rice]].\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Melt 2 tablespoons of the [[Butter|butter]] in a pan over a medium heat until it starts to [[Brown|brown]].\n| Add half of the [[Onion|onion]], [[Garlic|garlic]], and then the [[Rice|rice]].\n| Stir until the [[Grains|grains]] of [[Rice|rice]] are coated with the [[Butter|butter]] and add the water.\n| Reduce the heat to low, cover and allow to cook until the [[Rice|rice]] has absorbed the water - about 15 minutes.\n| Meanwhile, melt the remaining 1 tablespoon [[Butter|butter]] in a separate pan and add the remaining half of the [[Onion|onion]] and the [[Chorizo|chorizo]].\n| Allow to cook briefly and add the remaining ingredients. \n| When the ingredients in both pans are cooked, mix together and serve.\n| Alternatively, you can layer them in a serving dish or [[Mould|mould]] and turn out onto a large platter.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nA complete meal in itself, arroz rico can also be served as an accompaniment to other dishes.\n===Chef's notes===\n'Encurtido en mostaza' literally means '[[Pickled|pickled]] in [[mustard]]'.  It is similar to the British [[piccalilli]], but the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] are chopped much smaller.  I have not found anywhere in the UK that sells it, so would suggest that you use [[piccalilli]] and chop the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] very finely.  Try to avoid certain well known brands of Mustard pickle as they won't be gutsy enough.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Arroz tico]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Arroz tico]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Arroz tico]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Arroz tico]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Arroz tico]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes|Arroz tico]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes|Arroz tico]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Arroz tico]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#arroztico #rice #butter #onion #garlic #vegetables #chorizo #piccalilli #miseenplace #redpeppers #mould </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Atole",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Atole: Cooking Wiki\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#atole #masa #cornmeal #chocolate #riceflour #fruit #cornstarch #toasted #beverages #piloncillo #vanilla \n|hashtagrev=12032020\n|description=Atole is a traditional cornstarch-based Mexican and Central American (where it is known as atol) hot drink\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n[[Image:Mas vale atole.jpg|300px|thumb|right|M\u00e1s vale atole con risas, que chocolate con l\u00e1grimas]]\n'''Atole''' is a traditional [[cornstarch]]-based Mexican and Central American (where it is known as atol) hot drink. [[Chocolate]] atole is known as champurrado. It is typically accompanied with [[tamales]], and very popular during the Christmas holiday season (Las Posadas).\n\nThe drink typically includes [[masa]] ([[corn meal]]), water, [[piloncillo]], [[cinnamon]], [[vanilla]] and optional [[chocolate]] or [[fruit]]. The mixture is blended and heated before serving. The resulting blends vary in texture, ranging from a porridge to a very thin liquid consistency. Atole can also be prepared with [[rice flour]] or [[oatmeal]] in place of [[masa]]. In northern Mexico there is also a variation using pinole (sweetened toasted corn meal). Although atole is one of the traditional drinks of the Mexican holiday Day of the Dead, it is very common during breakfast and dinnertime at any time of year. It is usually sold as street food.\n\nOther derivations exist. In New Mexico, blue corn atole is finely ground [[cornmeal]] [[toasted]] for cooking, consumed as a grainy porridge-style drink served warm, usually sweetened with [[sugar]] and/or thinned with [[milk]]. It is usually served at breakfast like cream of wheat or oatmeal. It is said that elders would drink Atole because it gave them energy and if a mother is nursing it gives them more [[milk]]. \n\nSalvadoran varieties include atol shuco (\"dirty\" atol, a reference to its darker colour), particularly popular in the Caba\u00f1as region.\n{{CategoryLineIngredients}}\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Beverages]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Non-alcoholic beverages]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#atole #masa #cornmeal #chocolate #riceflour #fruit #cornstarch #toasted #beverages #piloncillo #vanilla </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

title": "Caipirinha",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Caipirinha recipe Accompaniments \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#caipirinha #muddle #cachaca #rollingpin #sugarcane #granulatedsugar #rum #lime #limes \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Caipirinha is Brazil's national cocktail, made with cachaca, sugar and lime. Cachaca is Brazil's most common distilled alcoholic beverage\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 85\n|PortionCalories = 85\n|DatePublished=12th April 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Servings: 1 - Makes 1 cocktail\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 2 minutes\n |PrepTime = 2 minutes\n |CookTime = None\n |Image = [[Image:Caipirinha cocktail recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Brazilian rum</span>\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">The country persons drink</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n===What is caipirinha?===\n'''Caipirinha''' is Brazil's national cocktail, made with [[cacha\u00e7a]], [[sugar]] and [[lime]]. [[Cacha\u00e7a]] is Brazil's most common distilled alcoholic beverage. Like [[rum]], it is made from sugarcane. Cacha\u00e7a is made from [[sugarcane]] alcohol, obtained from the fermentation of sugarcane juice which is afterwards distilled.\n\nOnce almost unknown outside Brazil, the drink has become more popular and more widely available in recent years, in large part due to the rising availability of first-rate brands of [[cacha\u00e7a]] outside Brazil. The International Bartender Association has designated it as one of their Official Cocktails.\nThe word \"caipirinha\" is the diminutive version of the word \"caipira\", which refers to someone from the countryside, being an almost exact equivalent of the American English hillbilly. The word may be used as either a masculine or a feminine noun, but when referring to this drink it is only feminine (usage of diminutives is conspicuous in Brazil). However, a Brazilian hardly ever thinks of a \"country person\" when ordering a \"Caipirinha\". In the mind of a Brazilian, the word \"Caipirinha\" is mostly associated with the drink itself.\n===Caipirinha cocktail recipe===\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1&frac12; [[limes]], chopped into cubes\n| 3 teaspoons white [[granulated sugar]]\n| Big handful ice cubes\n| 65ml/2&frac12;fl oz [[Cachaca]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the lime cubes and sugar to a cocktail mixer and using a [[muddle]] (or the end of a wooden [[rolling pin]]), mash the limes and sugar into a paste.\n| Add the Cachaca and some ice cubes, cover with a lid and shake 6-8 times.\n| Pour into a highball glass and serve.\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Beverages]]\n[[Category:Alcoholic beverages]]\n[[Category:Drink and beverage recipes]]\n\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#caipirinha #muddle #cachaca #rollingpin #sugarcane #granulatedsugar #rum #lime #limes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

title": "Cajun Pulled Pork",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Cajun Pulled Pork recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#lemon #cajunpulledpork #porkshoulder #onions #salad #pork #muscovadosugar #cajunseasoning #tapa #spice #redonions \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I am experimenting with spice mixes from Taste Sensation Ltd; their Tex Mex rub was wonderful, I arranged to get samples of their popular blends.\n|og:image=https://www.cookipedia.co.uk/wiki/images/thumb/d/db/Cajun_Pulled_Pork_recipe.jpg/450px-Cajun_Pulled_Pork_recipe.jpg\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=6th December 2019\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  8 hours, 10 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  8 hours\n|TotalCalories = 3863\n|PortionCalories = 1931\n|Image = [[Image:Cajun Pulled Pork recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">I'm a fan</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I just love Taste Sensation's spices.  Makes this recipe dead easy.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nI am experimenting with [[Spice|spice]] mixes from [[Taste Sensation Ltd]]; their Tex Mex marinade was wonderful so I arranged to get samples of their popular blends.\n\nAs this is an experiment I bought 1.4kg of [[pork shoulder]] and got the butcher to cut it into three slices.  This recipe uses one of those slices. I can use the other two to experiment with more of the [[Taste Sensation]] seasonings.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1400 g [[Pork shoulder|pork shoulder]]\n| 2 medium [[Red onions|red onions]], peeled and chopped\n| 1 [[Lemon|lemon]] cut into eight pieces\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Taste Sensation Cajun Seasoning]]\n| 200 ml [[red wine]]\n| 1 tablespoon of [[muscovado sugar]]\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Cajun Pulled Pork ready to cook.jpg|Ready to cook\nImage:Cajun Pulled Pork Ingredients.jpg|Minimal, but high quality ingredients\nImage:Taste Sensation spices with added cats.jpg|A sample of Taste Sensation spices, with added cats\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Squeeze the [[Lemon|lemon]] to collect the [[lemon juice]] while retaining the [[lemon]] pieces\n| Pour the red wine and lemon juice over the [[Pork|pork]]\n| Sprinkle the [[Taste Sensation Cajun Seasoning]] over the pork\n| Line the [[Slow Cooker|slow cooker]] with the chopped [[Onions|onions]] and [[Lemon|lemon]] pieces\n| Lay the [[Pork shoulder|pork shoulder]] over the [[Lemon|lemon]] and [[Onions|onions]]\n| Sprinkle the [[muscovado sugar]] over everything\n| Slow cook on medium heat for 8 hours, turning now and then\n| If it looks to be drying out too much add a little extra liquid, water or beverage of your choice!\n| If you are able, about halfway through remove the rind and excess fat, together with the lemon pieces\n| After eight hours, shred the [[Pork|pork]] with two forks and mix into the gravy\n| Serve!\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nThere are lots of great ways to serve [[Pulled pork|pulled pork]]:\n\n* In rolled up soft [[Flour tortillas|flour tortillas]] with crispy [[Lettuce|lettuce]] and [[Onions|onions]]\n\n* In [[Taco shells|taco shells]] with a [[Salad|salad]] mix and [[Sour cream|sour cream]]\n\n* As you would serve [[Roast pork|roast pork]]\n\n* As a [[Pizza topping|pizza topping]]\n\n* In a [[Burger|burger]] bun with a [[Salad|salad]]\n\n* As part of a [[Tapa|tapa]]\n===Chef's notes===\nThis was very, very good.  Impressed with the [[Cajun Seasoning]], not too hot but had tangy, herby notes. I needed to add a little extra liquid near the end, but only 50 ml or so. \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooked]]\n[[Category:Slow cooker recipes]]\n[[Category:Taste Sensation recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lemon #cajunpulledpork #porkshoulder #onions #salad #pork #muscovadosugar #cajunseasoning #tapa #spice #redonions </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Here is a fantastic [[Cornbread|cornbread]] recipe with a bit of a [[Caribbean]] twist - [[Pineapple|pineapple]]! . Give it a try and let me know what you think. I think it would be excellent with some [[Barbecued|barbecued]] jerk [[Chicken|chicken]] too.\"\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 cup [[All purpose flour|all purpose flour]]\n| 1 cup [[Cornmeal|cornmeal]] \n| 2 tablespoons [[Baking powder|baking powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 1 cup [[Butter|butter]], softened to room temperature\n| .75 cup [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 4 [[free range eggs]]\n| 1.5 cups canned [[Cream|cream]]-style [[Corn|corn]]\n| .5 cup canned crushed [[Pineapple|pineapple]], drained\n| 1 cup [[Shredded|shredded]] Monterrey jack [[Cheese|cheese]] or mild white [[Cheddar cheese|cheddar cheese]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3), [fan [[Oven|oven]] 140\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| [[Butter]] and [[Flour|flour]] a 9-inch square [[Glass|glass]] [[Cake|cake]] pan (you can use a metal pan but [[Glass|glass]] works better).\n| In a medium bowl, whisk together [[Flour|flour]], [[Cornmeal|cornmeal]], [[Baking powder|baking powder]] and [[Salt|salt]]; set aside.\n| Using an electric [[Mixer|mixer]], [[Cream|cream]] [[Butter|butter]] and [[Sugar|sugar]].\n| While [[Mixer|mixer]] is running, add [[Eggs|eggs]], one at a time, beating well after each addition.\n| Add [[Corn|corn]], [[Pineapple|pineapple]] and [[Cheese|cheese]]; mix to [[Blend|blend]].\n| At low speed, add [[Flour|flour]] mixture and mix until well blended.\n| Pour [[Batter|batter]] into pan and [[Bake|bake]] until golden [[Brown|brown]] around edges and a tester inserted in the center comes out clean, about 1 hour.\n}}\n===Variations===\nOptionally sprinkle some [[Scotch Bonnet Pepper]] or [[jalape\u00f1o peppers]] to add some fire.\n===Recipe source===\n{{RecipeCourtesyOfCubanCuisine}}\n===See also===\n* [[Hot Havana Cornbread (gluten free)]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cuban recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:CubanCuisine.co.uk]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#caribbeancornbread #butter #flour #pineapple #cornmeal #glass #bakingpowder #cheese #mixer #corn #cream </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Causa rellena",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Causa rellena recipe Cooking with chillies\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#causarellena #potato #shredded #lettuce #mould #lemonjuice #prawns #baking #ham #mashedpotatoes #mashed \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Causa is a popular Peruvian potato dish and its name comes from the Quechua word 'Kausay', meaning 'life'\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1762\n|PortionCalories = 440\n|DatePublished=14th July 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = 4\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = None\n |Image = [[Image:Causa rellena recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n======Best recipe review======\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Fancy-pants!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Wow, this has everything in it, plus potatoes!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> - [[User:Chef|Jerry]]</span></span>\n}}\nCausa is a popular Peruvian [[Potato|potato]] dish and its name comes from the Quechua word 'Kausay', meaning 'life'.  This particular recipe is typical of Peru's capital city, Lima and is also called '''Causa lime\u00f1a'''.  'Causa', meaning 'cause' does not have a culinary meaning in Spanish.  'Relleno/a' means stuffed.  In English language recipes, they are sometimes referred to as stuffed [[mashed potatoes]].  They are not really stuffed though, just layered.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.25kg cold [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled, [[Boiled|boiled]] and [[Mashed|mashed]] thoroughly\n| 125 ml [[Corn|corn]] or [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Aj\u00ed pepper|aj\u00ed amarillo flakes]], soaked in the oil\n| 180 ml [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] to taste\n| &frac14; of a [[Spanish]] [[Onion|onion]], cut into thin strips\n| 8 [[Black olives|black olives]], stones removed, and cut in half\n| 2 [[Eggs, hard-boiled|eggs, hard-boiled]], and each sliced into quarters\n| Stuffing of your choice: [[Shredded|shredded]] [[Chicken|chicken]], [[Tuna|tuna]], [[Ham|ham]], [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheese|cheese]], [[Avocado|avocado]], [[Sardines|sardines]] or [[Prawns|prawns]]\n| 1 crisp [[Lettuce|lettuce]], [[Shredded|shredded]]\n| Chopped [[olives]], [[peppers]] etc to garnish (optional)\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| To the cold mashed potatoes, add the oil, [[Aj\u00ed pepper|aj\u00ed amarillo flakes]], lemon juice and seasonings and mix until the potato is smooth and manageable.\n| You now need to layer the causas.  The easiest way to do this is use a [[Mould|mould]] with both ends open.\n| Grease the [[Mould|mould]] and taking one-eighth of the [[Potato|potato]] mixture, smooth out in the bottom of the mould.\n| Place 2 [[Egg|egg]] slices on top, followed by 4 [[Olive|olive]] halves and a quarter of the [[Onions|onions]].\n| Then add a layer of your chosen stuffing.\n| Finally add a further eighth of the [[Potato|potato]] mixture.\n| When unmoulded, repeat the same until you have 4 causas.\n| Add garnishes if desired.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nPlace the [[Shredded|shredded]] [[Lettuce|lettuce]] in the centre of a plate and gently unmould the causas on the top.\n===Variations===\nYou can make the whole thing in a greased [[Baking|baking]] dish if you have no moulds.\n===Chef's notes===\nThe quantity of [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] does seem rather excessive, but will give it a go and see what happens.  [[Aj\u00ed pepper|Aj\u00ed amarillo]] chillies are available from the [[South Devon chilli farm|South Devon Chilli Farm]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Causa rellena]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Causa rellena]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Causa rellena]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Causa rellena]]\n[[Category:Peruvian recipes]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes|Causa rellena]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Causa rellena]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Causa rellena]]\n[[Category:Starters|Causa rellena]]\n\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#causarellena #potato #shredded #lettuce #mould #lemonjuice #prawns #baking #ham #mashedpotatoes #mashed </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

This recipe is from Chile and is served with a spicy sauce\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 5608\n|PortionCalories = 701\n|DatePublished=20th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Chancho a la chilena, sliced - ready for the sauce\n |Servings = Serves 8\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 6 hours 25 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 6 hours 10 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Chancho a la chilena (Chilean pork loin) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Si</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Si, si!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Pork]] is a favourite [[Meat|meat]] throughout Latin America and many of their recipes use [[Pork loin|pork loin]].  This recipe is from [[Chile]] and is served with a spicy [[Sauce|sauce]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 60 ml [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 1.8 kg boneless [[Pork loin|pork loin]], in one piece\n| 2 medium [[Onions|onions]], sliced\n| [[Garlic]], to taste, chopped\n| 1 [[Carrot|carrot]], scraped and sliced\n| 1 [[Celery|celery]] stick, cut into 2.5 cm pieces\n| 1 [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Dried oregano|dried oregano]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Dried thyme|dried thyme]]\n| &frac14; teaspoon [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]]\n| Seasoning\n| 140 ml [[Red wine vinegar|red wine vinegar]]\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Chancho a la chilena cooked and cooling.jpg|Cooked and cooling\nImage:Ready to boil.jpg|Ready to boil\nImage:Chancho a la chilena (Chilean pork loin) basic ingredients.jpg|The basic ingredients\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a large pan and [[Brown|brown]] the [[Meat|meat]] lightly all over.\n| Add the remaining ingredients with enough water to cover.\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], cover, reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] gently until the [[Meat|meat]] is tender - about 3 hours.\n| Allow the [[Meat|meat]] to cool completely in the [[Stock|stock]] - this will take around 3 hours so allow for this when calculating cooking times.\n| Remove to a serving dish and reserve the stock for another use.\n| Serve the pork sliced and cover with [[Salsa de aj\u00ed colorado (Red pepper sauce)|Salsa de aj\u00ed colorado]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and [[Rice|rice]] or [[Potatoes|potatoes]].\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you are wanting to reduce the number of servings, you will have to pay particular attention to the [[Pork|pork]] cooking time, as smaller pieces will cook more quickly.\n\nMaking this recipe for 2 people, a whole [[pork loin]] is was impractical so I've adjusted the recipe (below) to use 1 large [[pork tenderloin]], about 560 g.  I have used fresh herbs where possible and have roughly chopped the vegetables as they won't be eaten afterwards.  I used about the identical quantities, topping up with water to cover. This version was cooked for 1 hour and took 3 more hours to cool. --[[User:Chef|Chef]] 15:13, 10 October 2010 (BST)\n===Chef's notes===\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chancho a la chilena (chilean pork loin)]]\n[[Category:Chilean recipes|Chancho a la chilena (chilean pork loin)]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Chancho a la chilena (chilean pork loin)]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chancho a la chilena (chilean pork loin)]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Chancho a la chilena (chilean pork loin)]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes|Chancho a la chilena (chilean pork loin)]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#porkloin #pork #boil #stock #redwinevinegar #sauce #celery #carrot #groundcumin #bayleaf #chile </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Chancho a la chilena - Chilean pork loin, a pressure cooker recipe",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chancho a la chilena Chilean pork loin, a pressure cooker recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#potatoes #pressurecooker #leeks #porkloin #celery #pork #pittabreads #onions #sage #parsley #chiledearbol \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Pork is a favourite meat throughout Latin America and many of their recipes use pork loin. This recipe uses a pressure cooker to produce tasty cold pork for salads\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1358\n|PortionCalories = 169\n|DatePublished=25th January 2015\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Slice once it is cold\n |Servings = Serves 8\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 4 hours 10 minutes\n |PrepTime = 3 hours 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour\n |Image = [[Image:Chancho a la chilena (Chilean pork loin) pressure cooker recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Pork, under pressure!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">The best way to cook it!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:pork out of pressure cooker.jpg|300px|thumb|After 1 hour in the pressure cooker]]\n[[Pork]] is a favourite [[Meat|meat]] throughout Latin America and many of their recipes use [[Pork loin|pork loin]].  This recipe is from [[Chile]] and is served with a spicy [[Sauce|sauce]].\n\nI really love this recipe, it is a great way to make really tasty pork to be slices when cold to use in salads.  The original recipe; [[Chancho a la chilena (Chilean pork loin)]] is simmered on the stovetop, but I thought it would be interesting to try pressure cooking this as it is a great way to concentrate the flavours of the herbs and spices in the meat.\n\nI've adapted this recipe for what was seasonally available and what was in our freezer at the time.  We always freeze spare  [[carrots]], [[onions]], [[celery]], [[leeks]] and [[wine]] so this is a great recipe to use for frozen ingredients as that are used only to impart flavour and will be discarded once the cooking has been completed.  This version is probably not authentically Chilean.  If you want the authentic ingredients, take a look at [[Chancho a la chilena (Chilean pork loin)]].\n\nYou need to make this in advance to allow the pork to cool, although there would be equally good hot.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 60 ml [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 1.4 to 1.8 kg boneless [[Pork loin|pork loin]], in one piece, rind removed\n| 2 [[leeks]], sliced\n| half a bulb of garlic, unpeeled\n| 2 [[Carrot|carrots]], roughly chopped\n| 1 [[Celery|celery]] stick, roughly chopped\n| 2 [[Bay leaf|bay leaves]]\n| A few sprigs of [[sage]] leaves\n| A small sprig of [[rosemary]]\n| A small sprig of [[thyme]]\n| A handful of fresh [[parsley]]\n| 3 whole [[chile de arbol]]\n| 140 ml [[Red wine]]\n| 200 ml [[orange juice]]\n| A pinch of [[salt]] and [[black pepper|pepper]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Sit trivet in the base of the pressure cooker, (not on the raised stand).  This holds the meat away from the base of the pan so it does not cook directly, but leaves enough room for a large joint of pork.\n| Using half of the vegetables, make a bed in the trivet.\n| Site the pork joint, meat side down on the vegetables.\n|Season with salt and pepper and sprinkle the remaining ingredients over the pork.\n| Pour in the wine and orange juice and add enough hot water to ensure there is 7.5 cm [3\"] of liquid in the base of the [[pressure cooker]].  Check the instructions on your cooker, some may have differing minimum liquid level requirements.\n| Seal the lid on the cooker and bring the cooker to pressure\n| Cook for 1 hour at medium to high pressure\n| Allow the [[pressure cooker]] to [[De-pressurising_a_pressure_cooker|depressurise naturally]]. \n| Let the cooker cool for an hour, so the meat can be handled, but before the fat has time to solidify.\n| remove the meat and place in a [[Lock and Lock box]] and allow to completely cool.\n| Discard the remaining contents of the pressure cooker.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nSlice the pork thinly and serve with a [[salad]] and cold [[potatoes]] or even [[pitta breads]]\nServe with [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and [[Rice|rice]] or [[Potatoes|potatoes]].\n\n===Chef's notes===\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Chilean recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Pork]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Pressure cooker recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes|Pork]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#potatoes #pressurecooker #leeks #porkloin #celery #pork #pittabreads #onions #sage #parsley #chiledearbol </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Cheatin' chicken enchiladas Cooking with chillies recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#cheatinchickenenchiladas #chicken #garlicoliveoil #fry #tortillas #tomatoes #celery #emmenthalcheese #dried #mushrooms #oliveoil \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This recipe is a great way of using leftovers\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3392\n|PortionCalories = 848\n|DatePublished=27th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4 with an accompaniment such as [[refried beans]]\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 1 hour\n|PrepTime = 30 minutes\n|CookTime = 30 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Cheatin' chicken enchiladas recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">So delicous</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">So blooming easy too!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis recipe is a great way of using up leftovers. It came about because I needed to use up a ([[frozen]]) carton of Waitrose green Thai [[chicken]] soup and also needed a photograph of [[enchiladas]].  \n\nThe ingredients were those to hand so you could easily meddle with them.\n\n'''If you are not using a spicy soup, then add a few finely chopped chillies (to taste) and either a can of chicken soup or some chicken stock that has been thickened with a tablespoon of flour.'''\n\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 220 g [[chicken]] fillets, chopped\n| 600g pot of green Thai chicken soup -  or 568 lm (1 pint) chicken stock, thickened with flour or cornflour\n| 150 g [[Emmenthal cheese]], [[grated]]\n| 2 sticks of [[celery]], chopped into thin crescents ''(half moons)''\n| 1 large [[onion]], peeled and sliced\n| 3 tablespoons [[garlic olive oil]] or [[olive oil]] and 1 [[garlic clove, crushed]]\n| 8 closed-cup [[mushrooms]], sliced thinly\n| 7 sun-[[dried]] [[tomatoes]], sliced (in [[oil]], with a little of the oil, if needed)\n| 1 teaspoon freshly ground [[white cumin]] seeds\n| 1 teaspoon [[dried]] [[oregano]] leaves\n| 1 green [[bell pepper]], sliced\n| 8 [[flour]] or [[corn tortillas]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]=== \n* Preheat the [[oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - Gas 4) \n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a [[wok]] or [[frying]] pan, heat the [[garlic olive oil]] gently and [[fry]] the [[celery]] and [[onions]] for about 5 minutes until softened\n| Add the [[mushrooms]] and sliced [[tomatoes]] and a little of the [[oil]] if needed\n| [[Fry]] for a few minutes\n| Tip in the chopped [[chicken]] fillets and the ground [[spices]] and cook until the chicken seems done\n| Add 100 g of the [[Emmenthal cheese]] and stir until melted and well mixed\n| Add the chopped [[peppers]] and stir without cooking any further\n| Divide the mix into eight portions and roll up in the [[tortillas]]\n| Place in an oven proof dish\n| Pour the soup over the [[tortillas]] and sprinkle with the remaining [[cheese]]\n| Bake for 30 minutes\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Cheatin' chicken enchiladas recipe3.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Sliced peppers added, cooked and ready to roll\nImage:Cheatin' chicken enchiladas recipe2.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Enchiladas with Waitrose green Thai soup\n</gallery>\n\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with a [[Mango salsa]] and [[sour cream]]\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Cookery cheats]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cheatinchickenenchiladas #chicken #garlicoliveoil #fry #tortillas #tomatoes #celery #emmenthalcheese #dried #mushrooms #oliveoil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Use it as a recipe template, almost any [[Meat|meat]] and certainly any favourite [[Soup|soup]] would work very well in this recipe.\n\nIt requires pre cooked [[Pork|pork]], so I used [[Sous vide Tex-Mex pork tenderloin fillet]], however, you could easily slice a [[Pork tenderloin fillet|pork tenderloin fillet]] and pan [[Fry|fry]] it instead.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| About 700g of pre cooked [[Pork tenderloin fillet|pork tenderloin fillet]] - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Pork fillet enchiladas baked.jpg|After 30 minutes at 180\u00b0 C \nImage:Pork fillet enchiladas soup added.jpg|Soup and cheese added\nImage:Pork fillet enchiladas rolled.jpg|8 pork Enchiladas, rolled\nImage:Pork fillet enchiladas ready to roll.jpg|Evenly filled and ready to roll\n</gallery>\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Add the filling ingredients to a bowl and mix really well.\n| Lightly [[Oil|oil]] the base of a [[Baking tray|baking tray]] with [[Olive oil|olive oil]].\n| Distribute the filling amongst the 8 [[Tortillas|tortillas]], adding the filling to all of them before rolling up takes the guesswork out of the amount needed for each [[Tortilla|tortilla]].\n| Roll the [[Tortillas|tortillas]] up and starting at one end of the tray, lay them fold side down so they don't unroll.\n| Pour the [[Soup|soup]] over the [[Tortillas|tortillas]] and jiggle the pan to ensure it gets between the rolls.\n| Top with 50 g of [[Cheddar cheese|cheddar cheese]] a drizzle of [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and a grate of [[Black pepper|black pepper]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a [[Salad|salad]] and a few sliced [[tomatoes]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Cookery cheats]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#oliveoil #soup #cheddarcheese #tortillas #porktenderloinfillet #pork #grated #corn #pulledpork #miseenplace #tortilla </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It is based on Jamie Oliver's recipe of the same name, though I recall having to adjust the quantities quite a bit from his original recipe.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 60 g [[Butter|butter]]\n| 2 large [[Onions|onions]], peeled and thinly sliced\n| 1 350g can of [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]] kernels, drained\n| 4 large [[Eggs|eggs]], beaten\n| 325 g coarse [[Yellow cornmeal|yellow cornmeal]]\n| 250 ml full [[Fat|fat]] [[Milk|milk]]\n| 1 heaped teaspoon [[Baking powder|baking powder]]\n| 6 tablespoons [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n| [[Sea Salt|Sea salt]] & [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 150 g strong [[Cheddar cheese|cheddar cheese]], [[Grated|grated]]\n| 3 fresh [[Green chillies|green chillies]], 2 deseeded and chopped finely, the other cut into thin rings\n| [[Olive oil]] for greasing\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Butter|butter]] to a [[Frying pan|frying pan]] or [[Wok|wok]], give it a good grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]] and gently [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] for 15 minutes\n| Once the [[Onions|onions]] are golden, carefully add the drained [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]]\n| [[Stir-fry]] the [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]] for a few minutes then remove the pan from the heat and set to one side.\n| Add the [[Eggs|eggs]], [[milk]], [[Cornmeal|cornmeal]], [[Flour|flour]], [[Baking powder|baking powder]], a pinch of [[Salt|salt]] and most of the [[Cheese|cheese]] (leaving a little to sprinkle on the top) and beat until really well mixed.\n| Stir in the onions and sweetcorn and mix again.  It helps to leave the mixure to rest for 10 minutes after the first mix to allow the cornmeal to soak up the milk.\n| Grease two 22cm round flan sandwich tins with a little [[Olive oil|olive oil]], line the base with [[Greaseproof paper|greaseproof paper]] and pour in the [[Cornbread|cornbread]] mixture.\n| [[Bake]] for 20 minutes then carefully remove from the oven and sprinkle the top with the remaining sliced [[Chilies|chilies]] and [[Cheese|cheese]].\n| [[Bake]] for a further 10 minutes.\n| Remove from the [[baking tray]] and allow to cool on a wire rack for 15 minutes before serving.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Cheese and chilli cornbread ready to bake.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Cheese and chilli cornbread, ready to bake\nImage:Cheese and chilli cornbread ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The ingredients for cheese and chilli cornbread\n</gallery>\n\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot or cold\n===Chef's note===\nDon't forget the [[greaseproof paper]] or you will find it very hard to get the cornbread out of the tins. :-(\n==See also==\nThis recipe is based on a version of Jamie Olivers 'Chilli cheese cornbread' from ''Jamie's America'' ISBN 978-0718154769\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cheeseandchillicornbread #sweetcorn #onions #cheese #bakingpowder #bake #greaseproofpaper #eggs #cornbread #butter #oliveoil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This will take about 4 minutes a side\n| Keep warm while you cook the remaining pupusas\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[curtido]]\n===Variations===\n\nMake the pupusas with a combination of this, [[refried beans]] and the filling for [[Pupusa de Chicharron|Pupusa de Chicharr\u00f3n]] (bacon, tomaotes and green peppers)\n\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Starters|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#curtido #cheesepupusas #cheeses #springonions #unusualrecipes #corntortillas #cheddar #refriedbeans #masaharina #toasted #grated </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chili con carne a beef recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#beef #chocolate #onion #tomatoes #rice #vegetables #garlic #simmer #frying #tortillas #dried \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is the recipe my husband and I developed over time and it's very tasty and fairly healthy\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2146\n|PortionCalories = 357\n|DatePublished=20th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 1 hour 15 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 1 hour\n|Image = [[Image:Chilli Con Carne recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Like mama used to make</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.35</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Specially with the chockolate</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is the recipe my husband and I developed over time and it's very tasty and fairly healthy.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500g best mince (ground [[Beef|beef]])\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], chopped\n| 1 - 2 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves\n| [[Extra virgin olive oil|extra virgin olive oil]]\n| [[Vegetables]] as available ([[Mushrooms|mushrooms]], [[Peppers|peppers]], [[Carrots|carrots]], [[Courgettes|courgettes]], for instance), chopped or sliced\n| 400g can chopped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 400g can [[Red kidney beans|red kidney beans]] in unsalted water, drained\n| 1 - 2 [[green chillies]], deseeded and chopped\n| 1 - 2 teaspoons [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]] (freshly ground is best)\n| 1 - 2 teaspoons [[Dried|dried]] [[Oregano|oregano]]\n| 1 square of Lindt 85% [[Chocolate|chocolate]], or equivalent dark chocolate: ([[Green & Blacks Organic Chocolate]])\n| 100ml [[Beef|beef]] [[Stock|stock]] (can be made from a cube if necessary)\n| [[Salt]] & [[Pepper]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat a couple of tablespoons of [[Oil|oil]] in a saucepan.  [[Fry]] [[Onion|onion]].  After a few minutes add Crushed [[Garlic|garlic]].  Cover and continue [[Frying|frying]] until [[Onions|onions]] are translucent.\n| Add [[Meat|meat]] and [[Brown|brown]].\n| Add remaining ingredients and seasoning.\n| Bring to [[Boil|boil]].  Lower heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for  30mins to 1 hour, depending on how much you've made.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[Tortillas|tortillas]], [[Rice|rice]] or crusty [[Bread|bread]] and a side [[Salad|salad]].\n\n===Variations===\n\nBy increasing the proportion of [[Beans|beans]] and [[Vegetables|vegetables]], one pack of [[Meat|meat]] can be stretched to ten or twelve servings.  If you do this, increase the proportion of [[Herbs|herbs]], [[Spices|spices]] and [[Chocolate|chocolate]] accordingly.  If you don't want to use chocolate (which really is the secret ingredient), you can substitute a little [[White sugar|white sugar]] to bring out the flavour of the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]].\n\nIf you don't like food too spicy, cut down the green [[Chili|chili]] content.  I make it for my young son in this way and he loves it with [[Rice|rice]].\n\n===Chef's tip===\n\nI make a big pot a couple of times a year and each time freeze 15 - 18 double portions that can be microwaved quickly to give us a hot meal in about 15 mins at the end of the working day.  \n\nIf you use low-[[Fat|fat]] [[Beef|beef]], this meal is a healthy option, as it has no other source of [[saturated fat]] apart from the small amount of [[Chocolate|chocolate]].\n\n==See also==\n* {{ChiliConCarne}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beef #chocolate #onion #tomatoes #rice #vegetables #garlic #simmer #frying #tortillas #dried </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Glad I found this again.  Lovely.</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nTry this as a [[Starter|starter]] or a [[Dip|dip]] to serve with drinks.  Plain [[Tortilla chips|tortilla chips]] or [[Toasted|toasted]] [[Pitta|pitta]] strips make a great dip for this dish.   Make your own [[tortilla chips]] if you have the time.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 fresh [[Green chillies|green chillies]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| &frac12; [[Red onion|red onion]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 2 fat cloves of [[Garlic]]\n| 250 g strong [[Cheddar cheese|cheddar cheese]], [[Grated|grated]]\n| 250 g [[Jarlsberg cheese]] or [[Gruyere cheese]], [[Grated|grated]]\n| 50 ml [[Sour cream|sour cream]]\n| 150 ml [[Double cream|double cream]]\n| 2 large fresh [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 15 ml [[Tequila]]\n}}\n'''to serve '''\n* 200g Plain [[Tortilla chips|tortilla chips]] or [[Pitta|pitta]] strips\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Scorch the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Chillies|chillies]] and peel them using the technique shown here (for [[Red peppers|red peppers]])\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Rub the skins off the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Chillies|chillies]] - use rubber gloves if your skin is sensitive and don't run your eyes!\n| Slice the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[chillies]] and scoop out and discard the [[Seeds|seeds]]\n| Cut the chillies and tomatoes into thin strips\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a pan and gently [[Fry|fry]] the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Onions|onions]] for 5 minutes until soft\n| Turn down the heat and add the [[Cheese|cheese]], sour and [[Double cream|double cream]] and stir until the cheese has melted and combined.\n| Just before serving, mix in the [[Tequila|tequila]] and add the [[Tomato|tomato]] and [[Chilli|chilli]] strips.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe warm with [[Tortilla chips|tortilla chips]].\n\nTry and use plain, unsalted [[tortilla chips]] as most commercial tortilla chips are coated with a disgusting powder that purports to be flavouring, which masks the delicious corn flavour. If you do,find them, let me know where you get them from!\n===Variations===\nPowder &frac14; teaspoon [[Dried oregano|dried oregano]] and &frac14; teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] and sprinkle onto the surface before serving.\n\nSprinkle a little homemade [[Tex-Mex seasoning]] on the surface.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tortillachips #tomatoes #chilliesinagarlicandcheesesauce #chillies #garlic #tequila #doublecream #pitta #grated #jarlsbergcheese #cheese </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Any [[Ground|ground]] [[Spices|spices]] or [[Spice|spice]] mix may be substituted for the [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]].\n===Chef's notes===\nDo not be tempted to lift the saucepan lid which the [[Corn|corn]] is cooking.  It would also be advisable to wear [[Oven gloves|oven gloves]] when adding the corn.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chilli and lime popcorn]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Chilli and lime popcorn]]\n[[Category:Popcorn recipes|Chilli and lime popcorn]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Chilli and lime popcorn]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Chilli and lime popcorn]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Chilli and lime popcorn]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chilliandlimepopcorn #corn #chillipowder #lemonjuice #chili #limejuice #preservedlemons #ground #popping #popcorn #poppingcorn </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

to 1 teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] or to taste\n| 1 x 400g (14 oz) can of [[Plum tomatoes|plum tomatoes]], chopped\n| 142 ml (&frac14; pint) [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 1 teaspoon whole [[Grain|grain]] [[Mustard|mustard]]\n| 15 ml (1 tablespoons) [[Black treacle|black treacle]] or dark [[Molasses|molasses]]\n| 1 x 425 g (15 oz) can [[Red kidney beans|red kidney beans]], rinsed and drained\n| 1 x 425 g (15 oz) can black eye [[Beans|beans]], rinsed and drained\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 1 tablespoon chopped [[Parsley|parsley]]\n}}\n'''to garnish'''\n* 1 small [[Red pepper|red pepper]] or a few spring onions, chopped (optional)\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a pan, give it a good grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]] and then saut\u00e9 the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] until it softens and starts to take some colour, about 5 minutes.\n| Sprinkle the [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] over the [[Onions|onions]] and mix well.\n| Add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Stock|stock]], [[Molasses|molasses]], [[mustard]] and the [[Beans|beans]].  Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] vigorously, uncovered for 15 minutes stirring now and then.  Simmer for longer if you want a thicker consistency.\n| Add the chopped [[Parsley|parsley]] , taste and adjust the seasoning if necessary.  [[Simmer]] for a further 5 minutes.\n| [[Roasted red pepper|Roast the red pepper]], remove the seeds and pith and  chop into slices\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Chilli beans reducing.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Chilli beans reducing\nImage:Chilli beans the ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Chilli beans, the ingredients\n</gallery>\n\n===Serving suggestions===\nGarnish with chopped [[Red pepper|red pepper]], or [[Spring onions|spring onions]] and serve with [[Bread|bread]] or [[Boiled rice|boiled rice]]. title": "Chilli gravy",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chilli gravy, Barbecue recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chilligravy #onion #oliveoil #gravy #lardons #onions #stock #simmer #ground #masaharina #chillies \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=OK chilli freaks, here's a chance to excel!\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 865\n|PortionCalories = 216\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Servings: 4 - Makes 4 cups of [[Chilli|chilli]] [[Gravy|gravy]]\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 55 minutes\n |PrepTime = 5 minutes\n |CookTime = 50 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Chilli gravy recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Mmmm; chillies</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Saves me having to add chilli to normal gravy.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\n\nOK [[Chilli|chilli]] freaks, here's a chance to excel!  In common with [[Chillies|chillies]], chilli gravy goes with just about anything.\n\nIt is great over any [[Barbecued|barbecued]] [[Meats|meats]] and [[Sausages|sausages]] and mandatory for [[Tex-Mex]] meals.\n\nThe beauty is that you can tailor the flavours to suit your tastes.  It also freezes well in 'meal-sized' portions.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 3 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]] (or the less healthy [[Lard|lard]] option!)\n| 2 big [[Garlic cloves, peeled and crushed|garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]].\n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], peeled and sliced.\n| 2 tablespoons [[Lardons|lardons]] (or [[Home smoked bacon|home smoked bacon]], chopped).\n| Your own variety of [[Dried|dried]] [[Chillies|chillies]], powdered in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]]\n| &frac14; teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], [[Ground|ground]] in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]]\n| &frac14; teaspoon [[Dried|dried]] [[Oregano|oregano]]\n| 2 cups water\n| 2 cups [[Beef stock|beef stock]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Masa harina|masa harina]]\n| [[Sea salt]] to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Saut\u00e9 the [[Onions|onions]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Lardons|lardons]] on a medium heat in the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] until soft, about 7 minutes.\n| Add the [[Herbs|herbs]] and [[Spice|spice]] and mix well.\n| Add the liquids, just bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and immediately reduce to a [[Simmer|simmer]] and cook, uncovered for 30 minutes.\n| Use a little of the [[Stock|stock]] to mix the [[Masa harina|masa harina]] to a paste and then add back into the stock, whisk well and [[Simmer|simmer]] for another 10 minutes.\n| Taste and season with [[Salt|salt]] if required.\n}}\n===Variations===\nCheat, cheat, cheat!\n\nI found half a pot of commercial [[Onion|onion]] [[Gravy|gravy]] in the [[Freezer|freezer]] which prompted this recipe. (I wanted something to liven up some [[Meatballs|meatballs]]).\n\nIf you are starting with a ready-made ([[Onion|onion]]) [[Gravy|gravy]], just omit the [[olive oil]], [[lardons]], [[Onions|onions]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Stock|stock]] and water.\n===Chef's note===\nProbably not at all authentic, but the juice of 1 [[lime]], 2 teaspoons of [[brown sugar]] and a tablespoon of [[tomato puree]] rounds this off nicely.\n==See also==\n* Many other [[gravy recipes]]\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Cookery cheats]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chilligravy #onion #oliveoil #gravy #lardons #onions #stock #simmer #ground #masaharina #chillies </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }

title": "Chimichurri",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chimichurri: Cooking Wiki\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chimichurri #chimichurrirecipe #latinamericanrecipes #vegetarianrecipes #dipsandsauces #spicyrecipes #veganrecipes #grilled #chillipepperrecipes \n|hashtagrev=12032020\n|description=Chimichurri is a sauce and marinade for grilled meat originally from Argentina but used in countries as far north as Nicaragua\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n[[Image:I Believe I can Fry Cimichurri.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Chimichurri]]\n'''Chimichurri''' is a sauce and marinade for [[grilled]] [[meat]] originally from Argentina but used in countries as far north as Nicaragua.\n\nChimichurri (also spelled Chimmichurri) originated in Argentina and is a popular sauce used with grilled meat in many Latin American countries. It is told that the unusual name comes from 'Jimmy McCurry', an Irishman who is said to have first prepared the sauce. He was marching with the troops of General Jasson Ospina in the 19th Century, sympathetic to the cause of Argentine independence. The sauce was popular and the recipe was passed on. However, 'Jimmy McCurry' was difficult for the native people to say. Some sources claim Jimmy's sauce's name was corrupted to 'chimichurri', while others say it was changed in his honour.\n\n==See also==\n* [[Chimichurri recipe|Chimichurri made conventionally]]\n* [[Chimichurri (TM)|Chimichurri made with a Thermomix]]\n* www.ibelieveicanfry.com/2012/04/grilled-skirt-steak-with-chimichurri.html Grilled Skirt Steak with Chimichurri (I Believe I Can Fry)\n{{disambig}}\n{{CategoryLineIngredients}}\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#chimichurri #chimichurrirecipe #latinamericanrecipes #vegetarianrecipes #dipsandsauces #spicyrecipes #veganrecipes #grilled #chillipepperrecipes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
