Chimichurri (also spelled..\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1225\n|PortionCalories = 204\n|DatePublished=31st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Chimichurri dip\n|Servings = Servings: 6 - Makes approximately 1 cup of [[sauce]]\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 1 hour\n|PrepTime = 1 hour\n|CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Chimichurri.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Jimmies Sauce</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Jimmy!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Chimichurri''' is a sauce and marinade for [[grilled]] [[meat]] originally from Argentina but used in countries as far north as Nicaragua.\n\nChimichurri (also spelled Chimmichurri) originated in Argentina and is a popular sauce used with grilled meat in many Latin American countries. It is told that the unusual name comes from 'Jimmy McCurry', an Irishman who is said to have first prepared the sauce. He was marching with the troops of General Jasson Ospina in the 19th Century, sympathetic to the cause of Argentine independence. The sauce was popular and the recipe was passed on. However, 'Jimmy McCurry' was difficult for the native people to say. Some sources claim Jimmy's sauce's name was corrupted to 'chimichurri', while others say it was changed in his honor.\n\n'''Chimichurri''' can be used as a condiment or as a [[marinade]] for [[grilled]] [[meats]].  It originates in South America and is frequently used in [[TexMex recipes]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| &#189; Cup [[Olive]] [[Oil]]\n| &#188; Cup Red [[Wine]] [[Vinegar]]\n| &#188; Cup Water\n| 1 small bunch flat leaf-[[parsley]] chopped finely\n| 4 cloves [[Garlic|garlic]] peeled and crushed\n| &#189; of a sweet [[red pepper]], deseeded and finely chopped\n| 1 [[tomato]]; peeled, deseeded, finely chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [[dried]] [[oregano]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[paprika powder]]\n| 1 [[Bay leaf]] chopped finely\n| 1 tablespoon [[sea salt]]\n| 1 teaspoon freshly ground [[ground black pepper]]\n| 2 tablespoons hot [[chili flakes]] (or to taste)\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a large bowl, add all of the ingredients except for the [[oil]] and [[vinegar]] and mix well\n| Leave to stand and amalgamate for 30 minutes\n| Add the [[vinegar]] and [[oil]], whisk well and allow to stand for a further 30 minutes\n| Pour the mixture into a suitable [[sterilised jar]] and refrigerate for 3 days prior to use for best results\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nAlthough it is ready after 1 hour it is at its best after at least 3 days.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#vinegar #grilled #chimichurrirecipe #marinade #texmexrecipes #paprikapowder #sauce #parsley #sterilisedjar #groundblackpepper #chiliflakes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

I prefer to use chicken legs because of the extra flavour you get when meat is\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2250\n|PortionCalories = 562\n|DatePublished=15th May 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 3\n|TotalTime = 1 hour\n|PrepTime = 25 minutes\n|CookTime = 35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Mole poblano recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Sounds weird!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">However, it tastes really good.  Just don't use Cadbury's Dairy Milk for this!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\n\nThis is my version of [[mole poblano]] chicken or [[chocolate]] [[chilli]] chicken.\n\nI prefer to use [[chicken]] legs because of the extra flavour you get when meat is cooked on the bone.\n\nI have been messing around with the ingredients for the [[mole]] so it's not totally authentic. Don't be afraid to experiment with the ingredients - the only thing I would not use is sweet [[milk]] chocolate!\n\nI did actually have [[tomatillos]] that I grew in a Grow-bag with my tomatoes. They were pretty meagre but it's nice to put them to a good use.  Remove the outer covering (husks) before use.\n\nThis was a total success.  Next time I would make double the sauce and freeze the other half as I think the [[mole]] would be good on steak too!\n\n\n'''For the [[boiled]] [[chicken]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 [[chicken]] legs, skin removed\n| 1 [[onion]], peeled and halved\n| [[Salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n'''for the mole [[poblano]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 [[chipotle chillies]], (deseeded if you don't want it too hot)\n| 1 dried [[:Image:Chilesdearbol.jpg|Chile de \u00e1rbol]].\n}}\n(''Don't be afraid to experiment with whatever other chillies you can get hold of'')\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| &#189; a large onion, chopped\n| &#189; teaspoon [[black peppercorns]]\n| 2 [[clove]] buds\n| &frac14;  teaspoon dried [[oregano]] or [[marjoram]]\n| A very small piece of [[cinnamon stick]]\n| &#189; teaspoon of [[fennel seeds]]\n| &#189; teaspoon of [[cumin seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon of [[coriander seeds]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[sesame seeds]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[ground almonds]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[raisins]]\n| 2 [[cloves garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| &frac14; cup [[breadcrumbs]]\n| 2 [[tortillas]], torn into small pieces\n| 5 tomatillos or [[tomatoes]] such as [[sungold]]\n| 25 g (1 oz) [[Green & Blacks Organic Chocolate]], unsweetened (I added a bit more at the end - taste and see first!)\n| 1.5 cups [[chicken stock]]\n}}\n\n'''To garnish'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 tablespoon [[sesame seeds]], lightly [[toasted]]\n| 1 [[orange]], quartered\n\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Simmering mole poblano.jpg|Mole poblano, simmering\nImage:Mole poblano ingredients.jpg|The mole ingredients\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n'''Mole poblano'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Don't be too fussy with the chopping as it's all going in the [[blender]] in the end.\n| Blitz all of the dry [[spices]] except for the sesame seeds to a powder in a [[coffee grinder]] or [[blender]] spice attachment\n| Add the remaining ingredients to the [[blender]] and blitz to a smooth sauce\n| Tip the dried spice mix into the sauce and give it a final blitz.\n| Pour the sauce into a pan, bring to a simmer and continue to simmer for 30 minutes stirring now and again\n}}\n\n'''Cooking the chicken legs'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the [[chicken]] legs in a pan with the onion halves and cover with boiling water, seasoning with salt and pepper\n| Return to the boil, then cover and simmer for 25 minutes\n}}\n\n'''Combining the two'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Remove the chicken legs and drain\n| Add the chicken to the mole (sauce) and heat for a further 10 minutes\n| Meanwhile, toast 1 tablespoon of sesame seeds in a small pan\n| Transfer the [[mole poblano]] and [[chicken]] to a serving dish and sprinkle with the toasted [[sesame seeds]]\n| Enjoy Mexico's national dish!\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[plain boiled rice]], [[guacamole]] and [[sour cream]] or [[creme fraiche]] and maybe a few [[tortillas]] and a [[green salad]].\n\n===Chef's note===\n\nI could not get Mexican [[chocolate]] so used Green & Blacks organic [[chocolate]], which is bitter and not too sweet. After all, the dish has [[raisins]] or [[sultanas]] which have a little [[sugar]] anyway.\n\n===Recipe too complicated?===\n\nIt's not really, but if you really can't be doing with all these ingredients, I have seen bottles of [[mole sauce]] in some of the larger supermarkets.  \n\nTry it out with the pre-made sauce, then come back and make the real thing!\n\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n* {{ChiliConCarne}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #blender #chocolatechillichicken #sesameseeds #chocolate #mole #raisins #tortillas #molepoblano #sungold #breadcrumbs </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

title": "Cochinita pibil",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Cochinita pibil, Garlic recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#cochinitapibil #marinade #chillies #roast #tequila #onion #foil #bayleaves #pork #julienned #roasting \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Cochinita pibil, puerco pibil or Mexican pit-pork is a traditional Mexican slow-roasted pork dish from the Yucatan. Preparation of traditional\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4404\n|PortionCalories = 734\n|DatePublished=28th July 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 day, 5 hours\n |PrepTime = 1 day, 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 4 hours 45 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Cochinita pibil recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Firepit Pork</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Mexican Perfection.  Lots of lime, lots of chili, lots of annatto!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Cochinita pibil''', '''puerco pibil''' or '''Mexican pit-pork''' is a traditional [[Mexican]] slow-roasted pork dish from the Yucat\u00e1n.\n\nPreparation of traditional cochinita or puerco pibil involves [[marinating]] the [[meat]] in strongly acidic [[citrus juice]], colouring it with [[annatto seed]], and [[roasting]] the [[meat]] while it is wrapped in banana leaf. [[Tin foil]] now provides a modern substitute.\nTraditionally, cochinita pibil was buried in a pit with a fire at the bottom to [[Roast|roast]] it. The Mayan word \"pibil\" means \"buried\".\n\n\n'''Grind to a powder'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2.5 tablespoons [[Annatto seeds|annatto seeds]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] \n| 1.5 teaspoons [[Peppercorns|peppercorns]] \n| 1/2 a teaspoon of [[allspice powder]] or 8 [[Allspice berries|allspice berries]] \n| 5 whole [[Cloves|cloves]]\n| 1/2 a teaspoon of [[dried oregano]] \n}}\n'''[[Marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and roughly chopped\n| 2 [[Scotch bonnet chili peppers]] (or [[Chillies|chillies]] of choice) \n| 80 ml [[Orange juice|orange juice]] \n| 80 ml [[Red wine vinegar|red wine vinegar]] \n| 1 tablespoon (30 ml) [[Salt|salt]] \n| 8 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled. \n| [[Juice|juice]] of 3 [[Lemons|lemons]] \n| splash of [[Tequila|tequila]]\n| 2 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| 1.3 kg [[Pork shoulder|pork shoulder]] \n}}\n'''Misc'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| Aluminium [[Foil|foil]]\n| 12 [[Taco shells]], or [[Tortillas|tortillas]] for serving\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Add the [[Spices|spices]] to a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] or [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]] and grind to a powder.\n* De-[[Seed|seed]] and roughly chop the [[Chillies|chillies]]\n* Add the [[Onion|onion]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Citrus|citrus]] juices, [[Vinegar|vinegar]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Spice|spice]] powder to a [[Blender|blender]] and liquidise.\n* Remove and discard the [[Pork rind|pork rind]] and cut the [[Pork|pork]] into 5cm (2\") cubes. Retain some of the [[Fat|fat]].\n* Place the [[Marinade|marinade]] ,[[bay leaves]] and the [[Pork|pork]] in a large [[lock and lock]] box or [[Tupperware]] container, shake well and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 24 hours, mixing now and then.\n* For a little extra flavour, quarter the juiced [[lemons]] and add then to the marinade, discard before cooking.\n\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3) (see Chef's note)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Line a large [[Roasting|roasting]] tin with a large sheet of [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]].\n| Add the [[Meat|meat]] and [[Marinade|marinade]] and seal with the [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]]. [[Banana leaves]] can be used here, though it is still an idea to use tin-[[Foil|foil]] to provide a really good seal.\n| [[Roast]] for 4.5 hours.\n| Remove the [[Meat|meat]] and rest for 15 minutes.\n| Shred with a fork.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Cochinita pibil marinade.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Cochinita pibil marinating\nImage:Cochinita pibil ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The ingredients for cochinita pibil\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nAs far as I can ascertain, the traditional way to serve this would be whole on [[plain rice]] with a salad and [[black beans]] or to shred the meat and serve in a rolled [[flour tortilla]] with a little [[salsa]].\n\nWhen we had this, somewhat unconventionally, we treated Cochinita pibil as you would [[Peking duck]].  Shred the pork, serve with [[julienned]] [[spring onions]], [[julienned]] [[cucumber]], [[green salad]], halved [[flour tortillas]], [[sour cream]], [[garlic mayonnaise]] and a variety of Chinese [[sauces]] such as [[plum sauce]], [[hoisin sauce]] etc.  Spread a [[tortilla]] with [[dips of your choice]], add a little salad and shredded pork, roll up and devour.  An absolute and total success!\n\nThe fourth time I cooked this, we ate half of it 'Chinese style' and made a wonderful curry with the second half. Just fried up some onions, celery, garlic with my favourite [[curry paste]], added a can of [[coconut milk]] and a can of [[chick-peas]] simmered it for an hour or so and served it with rice and peas. That stretched it out for another 2 days!    \n\n===Variations===\nI had no [[tequila]] so used [[dark rum]] instead.\nIn Mexico we use sour orange juice, not the regular oranges, but you can use only lemon juice and vinegar.\n\n===Chefs' note===\n2 unseeded [[Scotch bonnet chili peppers]] made this dish very hot, delicious,but bearable.  Remove the seeds if you don't want it too hot, or use a different [[chilli]].\n\nIf you have made the dish very (chili) hot, it's probably a good idea to separate the meat from the sauce before shredding the meat and serve the sauce separately.  For the sake of you heart, leave it to settle for a bit then drain most of the fat off.  It will be just as delicious, but much better for you.\n\nHaving made this a number of times, I now follow Jamie Oliver's idea for cooking [[slow roast lamb]], let the [[oven]] reach its highest setting, the moment you put the meat in the oven, reduce the heat to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3).\n====No chillies in authentic Mexican cochinita pibil====\nYou can avoid using chilli, in Mexico, Cochinita Pibil is not hot at all, we don't use any chilli. -- [[User:Myrna_Amor_Miranda]]\n{{Template:See-also-pulled-pork}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cochinitapibil #marinade #chillies #roast #tequila #onion #foil #bayleaves #pork #julienned #roasting </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Cochinita pibil (slow cooker recipe)",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title= Cochinita pibil - A Mexican slow-cooker recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#pork #chillies #bayleaves #onion #tequila #marinade #cochinitapibil #lemons #garlic #julienned #lockandlock \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Cochinita pibil, puerco pibil (Mexican pit-pork) is a fantastic traditional Mexican slow-roasted pork dish from the Yucat\u00e1n. Ideal for use in a slow-cooker (crockpot)\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4379\n|PortionCalories = 729\n|DatePublished=13th July 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 day, 8 hours, 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 1 day, 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 8 hours\n |Image = [[Image:Cochinita pibil recipe slow cooked.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">May favourite meal</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.82</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Especially cooked so slowley</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Cochinita pibil''', '''puerco pibil''' or '''Mexican pit-pork''' is a traditional [[Mexican]] slow-roasted pork dish from the Yucat\u00e1n.\n\nPreparation of traditional cochinita or puerco pibil involves [[marinating]] the [[meat]] in strongly acidic [[citrus juice]], colouring it with [[annatto seed]], and [[roasting]] the [[meat]] while it is wrapped in banana leaf. [[Tin foil]] now provides a modern substitute.\n\nTraditionally, cochinita pibil was buried in a pit with a fire at the bottom to [[Roast|roast]] it. The Mayan word \"pibil\" means \"buried\".\n\nThis version is identical to the [[Cochinita pibil|original recipe]] except that is cooked in a slow cooker. \n\n\n'''Grind to a powder'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2.5 tablespoons [[Annatto seeds|annatto seeds]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] \n| 1.5 teaspoons [[Peppercorns|peppercorns]] \n| 1/2 a teaspoon [[allspice powder]] or 8 [[Allspice berries|allspice berries]] \n| 5 whole [[Cloves|cloves]]\n| 1/2 a teaspoon [[dried oregano]] \n}}\n'''[[Marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and roughly chopped\n| 2 [[Scotch bonnet chili peppers]] (or [[Chillies|chillies]] of choice) \n| 80 ml [[Orange juice|orange juice]] \n| 80 ml [[Red wine vinegar|red wine vinegar]] \n| 1 tablespoon (30 ml) [[Salt|salt]] \n| 8 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled. \n| [[Juice|juice]] and zest of 2 [[Lemons|lemons]] and one [[lime]] \n| splash of [[Tequila|tequila]]\n| 2 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[jaggery]] or [[muscovado sugar]]\n| 1.3 kg mixture of [[Pork shoulder|pork shoulder]] and [[Pork]] cheek.\n}}\n'''Misc'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 12 [[Taco shells]], or [[Tortillas|tortillas]] for serving\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Add the [[Spices|spices]] to a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] or [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]] and grind to a powder.\n* De-[[Seed|seed]] and roughly chop the [[Chillies|chillies]]\n* Add the [[Onion|onion]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Citrus|citrus]] juices, [[Vinegar|vinegar]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Spice|spice]] powder to a [[Blender|blender]] and liquidise.\n* Remove and discard the [[Pork rind|pork rind]] and cut the [[Pork|pork]] into 5cm (2\") cubes. Retain some of the [[Fat|fat]].\n* Place the [[Marinade|marinade]] ,[[bay leaves]] and the [[Pork|pork]] in a large [[lock and lock]] box or [[Tupperware]] container, shake well and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 24 hours, mixing now and then.\n* For a little extra flavour, quarter the juiced [[lemons]] and [[limes]] and add them to the marinade. Discard the lemons and limes before cooking.\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place in the [[slow cooker]] and cook for 8 hours on low.\n| Shred the meat with a fork and serve.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Cochinita pibil marinade.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Cochinita pibil marinating\nImage:Cochinita pibil ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The ingredients for cochinita pibil\n</gallery>\n\n===Serving suggestions===\nAs far as I can ascertain, the traditional way to serve this would be whole on [[plain rice]] with a salad and [[black beans]] or to shred the meat and serve in a rolled [[flour tortilla]] with a little [[salsa]].\n\nWhen we had this, somewhat unconventionally, we treated Cochinita pibil as you would [[Peking duck]].  Shred the pork, serve with [[julienned]] [[spring onions]], [[julienned]] [[cucumber]], [[green salad]], halved [[flour tortillas]], [[sour cream]], [[garlic mayonnaise]] and a variety of Chinese [[sauces]] such as [[plum sauce]], [[hoisin sauce]] etc.  Spread a [[tortilla]] with [[dips of your choice]], add a little salad and shredded pork, roll up and devour.  An absolute and total success!\n\nThe fourth time I cooked this, we ate half of it 'Chinese style' and made a wonderful curry with the second half. Just fried up some onions, celery, garlic with my favourite [[curry paste]], added a can of [[coconut milk]] and a can of [[chick-peas]] simmered it for an hour or so and served it with rice and peas. That stretched it out for another 2 days!    \n\n===Variations===\nI had no [[tequila]] so used [[dark rum]] instead.\n\n===Chefs' note===\n2 unseeded [[Scotch bonnet chili peppers]] made this dish very hot, delicious,but bearable.  Remove the seeds if you don't want it too hot, or use a different [[chilli]].\n\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n\nIf you have made the dish very (chili) hot, it's probably a good idea to separate the meat from the sauce before shredding the meat and serve the sauce separately.  For the sake of your heart, leave it to settle for a bit then drain most of the fat off.  It will be just as delicious, but much better for you.\n\nHaving made this a number of times, I now follow Jamie Oliver's idea for cooking [[slow roast lamb]], let the oven reach its highest setting, the moment you put the meat in the oven, reduce the heat to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3).\n==See also==\n* [[Cochinita pibil]] (same recipe, oven cooked)\n* [[The renowned Mr Brown Pulled Pork - Oriental]]\n* [[Beer pickled belly of pork]]\n* [[Pulled pork]]\n* [[Slow roast recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Slow cooker recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pork #chillies #bayleaves #onion #tequila #marinade #cochinitapibil #lemons #garlic #julienned #lockandlock </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Color chilena (Paprika oil) a vegetarian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#paprika #lard #garlic #bitter #vegetableoil #unusualrecipes \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This oil is very popular in Chilean cooking as it keeps indefinitely\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4420\n|PortionCalories = 276\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Servings: 16 - Makes about 350 ml\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 20 minutes\n |PrepTime = 5 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Color chilena (Paprika oil) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">The colour of this!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I was SO surprised to see how clear, and how colourful this was. \ud83e\udd13</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis [[Oil|oil]] is very popular in Chilean cooking as it keeps indefinitely\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500 ml [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| [[Garlic]] cloves, to taste, peeled and left whole\n| 6 tablespoons sweet [[Paprika|paprika]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] or [[Lard|lard]] in a saucepan and add the [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves.\n| Saut\u00e9 over a low to medium heat until the [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves are [[Brown|brown]], then remove them from the pan and discard.\n| Away from the heat, stir in the [[Paprika|paprika]] until it is mixed well with [[Oil|oil]].\n| Cool and pour into a sterilised bottle.\n}}\n===Variations===\nSometimes, this is made with [[lard]], in which case, use 450 g [[lard]] instead.\n===Chef's notes===\nMake sure that the [[Oil|oil]] is not on the heat when adding the [[Paprika|paprika]] as paprika turns [[Bitter|bitter]] if overcooked.  If you only wish to make a little of this oil, work on the basis that you will need 1 teaspoon of [[paprika]] to 2 tablespoons of [[oil]].  You end up with less [[oil]] than you started with as the [[paprika]] absorbs a lot of it and the [[oil]] is poured into the bottle leaving the [[paprika]] behind.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Color chilena (paprika oil)]]\n[[Category:Chilean recipes|Color chilena (paprika oil)]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Color chilena (paprika oil)]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters|Color chilena (paprika oil)]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Color chilena (paprika oil)]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#paprika #lard #garlic #bitter #vegetableoil #unusualrecipes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Congrio en fuente de barro",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Congrio en fuente de barro, Chilean recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#congrioenfuentedebarro #tomato #lemonjuice #parsley #fish #potatoes #cod #onion #paprika #beautifulWithBasa #sweetredpepper \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Literally 'Eel cooked in earthenware', this Chilean recipe does not actually include eel\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1760\n|PortionCalories = 440\n|DatePublished=19th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 50 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime =  40 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Congrio en fuente de barro.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Best with basa!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Lovely.  Living near Ely, I should have tried it with eels, but it was beautiful with basa!</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nLiterally '[[Eel]] cooked in earthenware', this Chilean recipe does not actually include eel.  The Chilean 'congrio' is ''Genypterus chilensis'' (red ling or red cusk eel) and its only similarity to the eel is that it has a large head and a tapering body.  Their habitat is restricted to Chilean and Peruvian coastal waters.  In the UK, [[Cod|cod]] is the best substitute\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 900 g [[Cod|cod]] fillets, each cut into 4 pieces\n| Seasoning\n| 2 tablespoons [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| 40 g [[Butter|butter]]\n| 1 teaspoon sweet [[Paprika|paprika]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], finely chopped\n| 4 medium [[Tomatoes, peeled|tomatoes, peeled]] and chopped\n| 450 g [[Potatoes|potatoes]], [[Boiled|boiled]] and sliced\n| 2 [[Hard boiled egg|hard boiled egg]], sliced\n| 1 [[Sweet red pepper|sweet red pepper]], seeded and cut into strips\n| 140 ml [[Milk|milk]] - if necessary\n| Chopped [[Parsley|parsley]] to garnish\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Season the [[Fish|fish]], place in a bowl and pour over the [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]].\n| Heat the [[Butter|butter]] in a [[Frying pan|frying pan]], stir in the [[Paprika|paprika]], add the [[Onion|onion]] and saut\u00e9 over a medium heat until the onion is soft.\n| Add the tomatoes and cook for a further few minutes.\n| Grease and earthenware dish or [[Casserole|casserole]] and add a layer of the [[Tomato|tomato]] mixture.\n| Then add a layer of [[Fish|fish]] and another layer of [[Tomato|tomato]].\n| Add a layer of [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and more [[Tomato|tomato]].\n| Repeat until all these ingredients are used up.\n| Top with the [[Eggs|eggs]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] strips.\n| Cover, and [[Bake|bake]] at 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4) for 30 minutes.\n| If it starts to dry out during cooking, add some [[Milk|milk]].\n| Serve, sprinkled with [[Parsley|parsley]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Salad|salad]] or [[Vegetables|vegetables]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Congrio en fuente de barro]]\n[[Category:Chilean recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes|Congrio en fuente de barro]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Congrio en fuente de barro]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Congrio en fuente de barro]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes|Congrio en fuente de barro]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes|Congrio en fuente de barro]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Congrio en fuente de barro]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Congrio en fuente de barro]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#congrioenfuentedebarro #beautifulWithBasa #tomato #lemonjuice #parsley #fish #potatoes #cod #onion #paprika #butter #sweetredpepper </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Makes about 10 [[tortillas]]\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 1 hour 35 minutes\n|PrepTime = 1 hour 20 minutes\n|CookTime = 15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Tortilla press2.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Delicious</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I love the special aroma of anything made with masa</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThese delicious [[corn tortillas]] are easy to make, though best made with a [[tortilla press]] if you can get hold of one.\n\nYou '''must''' use [[masa harina]] as [[cornmeal]] will not work.\n\n{{RecipeIngredientsTM\n| 250g [[masa harina]]\n| 330 ml hot water\n| 1/2 a teaspoon table [[salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place all of the ingredients into the bowl '''10 seconds / Speed 7''', then '''1 minute / Knead'''.\n| Rest for at least 1 hour then shape into 10 equal sized balls.\n| Using a [[tortilla press]] or [[rolling pin]], place a ball of dough between two non-stick sheets ([[Bake-O-Glide]] or similar) and press into shape\n| Heat a frying pan to a medium high temperature (but with no oil).\n| Cook each tortilla on one side for 15 seconds.\n| Turn and cook for 45 seconds.\n| Turn again and cook for a further 15 seconds.\n| They should have brown speckles.\n}}\n===Serving suggestion===\n\nCan be eaten as they are, fried, wrapped around [[beans]], [[salad]], [[chicken]], [[cheese]] etc.\n\nUse as suggested in your recipe\n*Make [[Cheese pupusas]] or [[Dobladas]] with your homemade [[maize tortillas]]\n===Variations===\n\nAdd 1-2 teaspoons [[chilli powder]] and/or 2-3 teaspoons [[garlic powder]] to the mixture.\n\n===Chef's note===\n\nIf you don't have a [[tortilla press]], use 2 chopping boards or just two sheets of wood as a substitute. These would go really well with our  [[Mango salsa]]\n\nQuesadillas are similar to the dish from San Salvador; [[Cheese pupusas|pupusas]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g (1 lb) fresh [[crabmeat]]\n| 1 packet of [[flour]] [[tortillas]] \n| 1 red [[sweet pepper]], cut into thin strips \n| 1 green [[sweet pepper]], cut into thin strips \n| &#189; a [[red onion]], peeled and thinly sliced\n| 1 tablespoon [[olive oil]] \n| 225 g (8 oz) [[mascarpone cheese]] \n| A good pinch of [[chilli powder]] \n| Good handful of [[coriander leaves]], finely chopped\n| 1 cup [[grated]] [[cheddar cheese]]\n| [[Culinary oil spray|Cooking oil spray]], I prefer [[olive oil]] for health reasons\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 230 \u00b0C (450 \u00b0F - Gas 8)\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[olive oil]] in a [[frying pan]]\n| Add the [[onions]] and [[peppers]] and [[fry]] until the [[onions]] are translucent \n| Meanwhile, into a large bowl, sift the [[crabmeat]] and remove any shell fragments\n| Stir the [[mascarpone cheese]] into the [[crabmeat]], add the [[coriander]] and [[chilli powder]] and mix well \n| Spray half of the [[tortillas]] with [[Culinary oil spray|cooking spray]]. Lay them [[oil]] side down on [[baking]] sheets \n| Add equal portions of the [[crabmeat]] and then [[onions]] and [[peppers]]\n| Sprinkle with the [[Cheddar cheese]]\n| Place the remaining [[tortillas]] on top and spray with cooking spray \n| [[Bake]] for about 10 minutes or until golden [[brown]]\n| Rest for 3 minutes then cut into quarters and serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with [[Mango salsa]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#crabmeat #tortillas #onions #oliveoil #peppers #culinaryoilspray #mascarponecheese #chillipowder #sweetpepper #cheddarcheese #crabquesadillas </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

[[Vanilla extract|vanilla extract]]\n| 3 tablespoons sweetened condensed [[Cuban coffee]] (espresso) \n| 275 g Goya [[Dulce de Leche]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\nHeat the oven to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3), [fan oven 140\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Place cookies in bowl of [[Food processor|food processor]]. Pulse 30 seconds, or until finely [[Ground|ground]]. (Or, place cookies in zip-top bag and using the bottom of a heavy [[Skillet|skillet]], pound cookies until finely crushed); transfer cookie crumbs to bowl (there should be about 2 cups).\n| Add [[Butter|butter]], stirring until combined. Transfer cookie mixture to 9\" spring form pan. Using your fingers, press cookie crumbs evenly onto bottom and sides of pan. [[Bake]] until firm and fragrant, 7 - 10 minutes; cool.\n| In the bowl of an [[Electric mixer|electric mixer]] on medium speed, beat [[Cream cheese|cream cheese]] until fluffy, about 3 minutes. Add [[Condensed milk|condensed milk]]; beat until smooth, 1 minute. Beat in [[Eggs|eggs]], [[Vanilla|vanilla]] and 3 tbsp. [[Dulce de Leche|dulce de leche]] and [[Cuban coffee]] until combined, 3 minutes.\n| Pour filling into prepared crust. \n| [[Bake]] until golden [[Brown|brown]] and set, but still wiggly in the middle, 45 - 55 minutes. Turn off [[Oven|oven]]; partially open [[Oven|oven]] door. Let [[Cake|cake]] sit in oven until room temperature, about 1 hour.\n| Transfer [[Cake|cake]] to [[Refrigerator|refrigerator]]; cool completely, at least 4 hours.\n| Remove [[Cheesecake|cheesecake]] from pan.\n| Place remaining [[Dulce de Leche|dulce de leche]] in zip-top bag. Using scissors, snip small hole in corner of bag. Applying even pressure on \"[[Pastry bag|pastry bag]],\" make swirly designs on top of [[Cake|cake]]; \n| slice and serve.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with fresh [[Cuban coffee]] of course!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cuban recipes]]\n[[Category:Jamaican recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Pies tarts and flans]]\n[[Category:CubanCuisine.co.uk]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n===Recipe source===\n{{Template:RecipeCourtesyOfCubanCuisine}}\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cubancoffee #cubancoffeedulcedelechecheesecake #dulcedeleche #cake #creamcheese #bake #eggs #condensedmilk #butter #miseenplace #electricmixer </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

of Cuban Cuisine UK\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 3\n|TotalTime =  3 hours, 35 minutes\n|PrepTime =  2 hours\n|CookTime =  1 hour, 35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Cuban guave and Carla?</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Guava Jello Pie!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\n\nThis authentic [[Cuban]] sweet pie recipe comes from [[Carla's]] grandmother and has some interesting Cuban ingredients.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n}}\n'''for the [[Pastry|pastry]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 5 oz. or 140 grams cold [[Butter|butter]], cut in small cubes\n| 9 oz. or 250 grams of [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n| 1 oz  or 100 grams [[Icing Sugar|icing sugar]]\n}}\n'''for the filling'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 9 oz or 250 grams of [[guava paste]]\n| 5 tablespoons fine [[Corn flour|corn flour]]\n| [[Juice|juice]] of one [[Lime|lime]]\n| 2 oz or 50 grams of [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 3 oz or 85 grams of [[Butter|butter]], cut into small cubes\n| 3 [[Egg yolks|egg yolks]]\n| 1 whole [[Egg|egg]]\n}}\n'''for the [[Meringue|meringue]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 5 [[Egg whites|egg whites]]\n| 9 oz or 250 grams [[Sugar|sugar]]   \n| 3 teaspoons [[Corn flour|corn flour]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6), [fan [[Oven|oven]] 180\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| For the [[Pastry|pastry]], [[Blend|blend]] the [[Butter|butter]] cubes and [[Flour|flour]] into small crumbs quickly so the [[Butter|butter]] stays cold. In a separate small bowl, combine [[Egg yolks|egg yolks]] with 2 tsbs. water, then [[Blend|blend]] into [[Flour|flour]] crumbs until [[Pastry|pastry]] reached right consistency...this may require a few more drop of water blended into the pastry.\n| Roll out cold [[Pastry|pastry]] on floured surface and place on to pie tin. Then [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 30 minutes.\n| Prick the bottom of [[Pastry|pastry]] pie bottom and heat [[Oven|oven]] to 200c/180c fan /gas  6 and [[Blind bake|blind bake]] for 15 minutes (my grandmother did not use [[Parchment paper|parchment paper]] or [[Beans|beans]] to keep the [[Pastry|pastry]] from rising..she just pricked the pastry several times right before putting it in the [[Oven|oven]].)\n| For the filling, slowly heat [[Guava|guava]] paste, 2 tablespoons of water, [[Sugar|sugar]] and [[Lime juice|lime juice]] for until just blended.  Remove from heat.\n| Add [[Butter|butter]] and beaten whole [[Egg|egg]] and [[Egg yolks|egg yolks]] to pan. Heat at medium, stirring vigorously for a few minutes until blended and then set the filling aside in the [[Refrigerator|refrigerator]].\n| For the [[Meringue|meringue]], whisk [[Egg whites|egg whites]] into stiff peaks, slowly add [[Sugar|sugar]], whisking as you add a bit at a time. Finally whisk in the [[Corn flour|corn flour]] until you have thick glossy peaks.\n| Pour the filling in the [[Pastry|pastry]] case, followed by the [[Meringue|meringue]].  [[Bake]] for 18 -20 minutes  until the [[Meringue|meringue]] is crisp and slightly coloured.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nLet the pie sit for at least an hour before serving.\n===Recipe source===\n* {{RecipeCourtesyOfCubanCuisine}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cuban recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Pies tarts and flans]]\n[[Category:CubanCuisine.co.uk]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pastry #butter #meringue #cubanguaveandlimemeringuepie #cornflour #eggyolks #eggwhites #blend #flour #egg #icingsugar </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

The recipe comes courtesy of Carla Cancio-Bello from [[Cuban Cuisine UK]].\n\nThis recipe can also be used to [[Roast|roast]] [[Chicken|chickens]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 3.6 kg whole [[Turkey|turkey]] (8 lbs)\n| 3 [[Cloves|cloves]] [[Garlic|garlic]] for [[Marinating|marinating]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Salt|salt]] for [[Marinating|marinating]] [[Turkey|turkey]]\n| &#189; lb. [[Black beans|black beans]]\n| 1 litre cups water\n| 2 slices [[Bacon|bacon]] cut in pieces (for base)\n| 6 slices [[Bacon|bacon]] whole  (for [[Turkey|turkey]] while [[Baking|baking]])\n| &#189; [[Onion|onion]] chopped\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]] cut in rings\n| &#189; [[Green pepper|green pepper]] chopped  for base\n| &#189; [[Green pepper|green pepper]] in strips  for cooking with [[Beans|beans]]\n| 375 ml white [[Rice|rice]] (1.5 cups)\n| 2 [[Cloves|cloves]] crushed  [[Garlic|garlic]] for [[Black beans|black beans]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Goya Adobo con pimienta]]\n| 125 ml sour [[Orange juice|orange juice]]\n| 1 large [[Green pepper|green pepper]]\n| 1 teaspoon of [[Black beans|black beans]]\n| 1 [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]]\n| 1/8 teaspoon [[Oregano|oregano]]\n| 125 ml [[Dry white wine|dry white wine]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3), [fan [[Oven|oven]] 140\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Clean the [[Turkey|turkey]] and remove the [[Parson's nose|parson's nose]].\n| Crush [[Garlic|garlic]] with [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]], [[Cumin|cumin]] and [[Oregano|oregano]].\n| Add [[Orange juice|orange juice]] and rub [[Turkey|turkey]] inside and out with this mixture.\n| Place [[Onion|onion]] rings on top and allow to [[Marinate|marinate]] for at least 2 hours and if possible overnight.\n| Wash [[Beans|beans]] and soak for a couple of hours.\n| Cook in the same water until soft. together with the [[Green pepper|green pepper]].\n| [[Fry]] the two slices of [[Bacon|bacon]] and in the same [[Fat|fat]] [[saut\u00e9]] the chopped [[Onion|onion]], [[Crushed garlic|crushed garlic]] and chopped [[Green pepper|green pepper]].\n| Add to the softened [[Beans|beans]]. Add washed [[Rice|rice]], [[Salt|salt]], [[Spices|spices]] and [[Bacon|bacon]].\n| Cook over medium heat until [[Rice|rice]] is dry but not quite done. It will finish cooking inside the [[Turkey|turkey]].\n| Stuff [[Turkey|turkey]] and sew up well.\n| Pour [[Wine|wine]] over  the [[Turkey|turkey]]  and place  the 6 slices of [[Bacon|bacon]] on top.\n| [[Roast]] for 3 hours at 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3)\n| [[Rest for]] 15 minutes before carving.\n}}\n===Variations===\nIf using [[chickens]] rather than a [[turkey]], use 4 x 900g (2 lb) chickens and roast for 1 hour at 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3). \n===Recipe source===\n{{RecipeCourtesyOfCubanCuisine}}\n==See also==\n* '''[[Meat cooking time calculator Metric|A comprehensive guide to roast meat cooking times]]''' - give the time you want to carve your roast and we'll give you a timed step by step roasting guide\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cuban recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:CubanCuisine.co.uk]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Marinaded]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#turkey #bacon #greenpepper #cubanstylestuffedroastturkey #onion #beans #garlic #rice #blackbeans #roast #marinating </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Dobladas",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Dobladas a cheese recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#dobladas #tortilla #tortillas #tortillapress #masaharina #cheese #rollingpin #cheddarcheese #panfried #dough #redpeppers \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Dobladas are folded, stuffed tortillas from Guatemala\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1694\n|PortionCalories = 169\n|DatePublished=20th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Doblada with salad\n |Servings = 10 dobladas\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Doblada with salad.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Glorious, Thanks Julia</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Cheese, masa, chillies.  What could be better.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nDobladas are folded, stuffed [[Tortillas|tortillas]] from Guatemala.\n\n\n'''For the [[Tortillas|tortillas]]:'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 330 ml hot water\n| 250 g [[Masa harina|masa harina]]\n}}\n\n'''For the filling:'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 150g [[Cheddar cheese]], [[Grated|grated]] or your favourite strong cheese\n| 2 [[Red peppers]], chopped\n| 2 small [[Onions]], chopped\n| Seasoning\n}}\n'''To cook:'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| [[Corn]] [[Oil|oil]]\n}}\n===Method===\n'''To make the [[Tortillas|tortillas]]:'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix the hot water with the [[Masa harina|masa harina]] - a [[Food processor|food processor]] is ideal as the water should be very hot.\n| Allow to cool and shape into 10 equal sized balls.\n| Using a [[Rolling pin|rolling pin]] or a [[Tortilla press|tortilla press]], shape into very thin disks.\n| Heat a [[Frying pan|frying pan]] to a medium high temperature.\n| Cook each [[Tortilla|tortilla]] on one side for 15 seconds.\n| Turn and cook for 45 seconds.\n| Turn again and cook for a further 15 seconds.\n| They should have [[Brown|brown]] speckles.\n| Reserve.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Frying a doblada.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Frying a doblada\nImage:Pressing the tortillas.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Pressing the tortillas\n</gallery>\n\n'''To make the dobladas:'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat some [[Oil|oil]] over a lowish heat in the same [[Frying pan|frying pan]].\n| Mix the filling ingredients together. \n| Place a [[Tortilla|tortilla]] in the pan and place some of the filling on one half of the tortilla.\n| When the [[Cheese|cheese]] has melted, fold the other half of the [[Tortilla|tortilla]] over the filling and serve.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nThese are normally served as [[Appetiser|appetisers]], allowing one per person, but would also make an excellent [[Main course|main course]].  Nice served with a simple [[Salad|salad]].\n===Variations===\nTry using [[Minced meat|minced meat]] instead of [[Cheese|cheese]].\n===Chef's notes===\nI have not specified any quantities for the filling as I feel that it is down to your own individual preference.\n\nIf you don't have a [[tortilla press]], use 2 chopping boards or just two sheets of wood as a substitute.  Place ball of [[dough]] between two non-stick surfaces such as small squares of [[Bake-O-Glide]] and stand on them!\n===Suppliers===\nSee the [[Tortilla Press]] page for UK suppliers.\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Dobladas]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes|Dobladas]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Dobladas]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Dobladas]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Dobladas]]\n[[Category:Starters|Dobladas]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Dobladas]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#dobladas #tortilla #tortillas #tortillapress #masaharina #cheese #rollingpin #cheddarcheese #panfried #dough #redpeppers </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Enfrijoladas recipe",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Enfrijoladas recipe Cheese, from Cookipedia.Co.Uk\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#enfrijoladasrecipe #chorizo #garlicoliveoil #tortilla #grapefruitsalsa #corntortillas #tortillas #refriedbeans #sourcream #montereyjack #cheddarcheese \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Enfrijoladas is a Tex-Mex dish that is similar to enchiladas\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3828\n|PortionCalories = 957\n|DatePublished=2nd April 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|ImageComment = Covered with melted [[Emmental]]\n|TotalTime = 1 hour 5 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 50 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Enfrijoladas recipe 2.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Tex Max at home</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.3</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This was easy to make and tasted fabulous - thank you!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nEnfrijoladas is a [[Tex-Mex]] dish that is similar to [[enchiladas]].  The [[tortillas]] are slightly [[fried]] and filled with [[frijoles refritos]] ([[refried beans]]) and [[pork]], or in this recipe spicy [[chorizo]].  I cheated with the refried beans as I didn't have time to soak them so I used canned, which are ok if but a little too salty.  I used [[Emmental cheese]], which is not authentic but I though it would work well. It did. This dish was a huge success.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 8 [[corn tortillas]]\n| 2 cans refried beans (or [[Refried beans recipe|homemade refried beans]])\n| 110 g (4 oz) [[grated]] [[Emmenthal cheese]], [[Monterey Jack]] or [[Cheddar cheese]]\n| 1/2 a small jar of [[Jalape\u00f1os|pickled jalape\u00f1os chillies]] or to taste\n| 150 ml to 200 ml (1/4 pint +) of [[beef stock|beef]] or [[vegetable stock]] \n| 120 g (4 oz) or a packet of spicy [[chorizo]], sliced\n| A handful of fresh [[coriander]], chopped\n| 8 tablespoons [[sour cream]]\n| [[Garlic olive oil]] for frying the [[corn tortillas]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4)\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a frying pan heat a few drops of [[garlic olive oil]] and fry each [[tortilla]] for a minute or so a side.\n| So you don't use too much oil, turn the first one over after a minute, put the next uncooked one on top of this to soak a little of the oil, flip them both. Remove the cooked one and repeat until they are all done. Add a few more drops of olive oil if the pan is too dry.\n| Divide the [[chorizo]] the cold contents of one cans of [[refried beans]] and layer each [[tortilla]] with an equal share as in the photo.\n| Lay them in an ovenproof dish\n| Heat the remaining tin of beans and add enough [[stock]] to make them ''pourable''. This way the bean ''sauce'' can get between the tortillas. Stir in the [[pickled jalape\u00f1os]]\n| Pour the bean mixture between the [[tortillas]], add a drizzle of [[garlic olive oil]] over the top and cover with the grated cheese\n| Bake in the over for 30 minutes and finish under the grill if you like your cheese toasty\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Enfrijoladas recipe 1.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Fill each tortilla with chorizo and refried beans\nImage:Grapefruit salsa.jpg|thumb|300px|right|[[Grapefruit salsa]]\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nGarnish with a dollop of [[sour cream]] on top and a sprinkle of coriander.\n\nDon your big hat and serve with a [[grapefruit salsa]] or [[curtido]] and a glass of ice-cold San Miguel!\n\n''The Mexican way: A tip from one of our Mexican visitors'' - You can also fill your enfrijoladas with shredded chicken and sprinkle some chopped or thinly sliced onion on top.  \n\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#enfrijoladasrecipe #chorizo #garlicoliveoil #tortilla #grapefruitsalsa #corntortillas #tortillas #refriedbeans #sourcream #montereyjack #cheddarcheese </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }

title": "Ensalada de coditos",
                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Ensalada de coditos, Egg recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#ensaladadecoditos #coditos #tuna #cream #mayonnaise #tomatoes #pasta #egg #parsley #tomato #blackolives \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A simple pasta salad with tuna, tomatoes, egg, Cream and mayonnaise\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1529\n|PortionCalories = 382\n|DatePublished=9th March 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 20 minutes\n|PrepTime = 5 minutes\n|CookTime = 15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Ensalada de coditos recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Any pasta is fine</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.1</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">While a purist would say this has to be made with coditos, any pasta is fine in this salad.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\n\nA simple [[Pasta salad|pasta salad]] with [[Tuna|tuna]], [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Egg|egg]], [[Cream|Cream]] and [[Mayonnaise|mayonnaise]].   [[Coditos]] are generally used in Mexico, but the combination of the other ingredients is typically [[Spanish]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 300 g [[coditos]] (pasta) - see Variations below\n| 130g tin of [[Tuna|tuna]] in [[Oil|oil]], [[Mashed|mashed]]\n| [[Home-made mayonnaise|Mayonnaise]], using 500 ml [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n|  2 tablespoons of [[single cream]]\n| 500g firm [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], thinly sliced\n| A handful of [[Black olives|black olives]], pitted\n| 1 [[Egg|egg]], hard [[Boiled|boiled]], finely chopped or put through a [[Sieve|sieve]]\n| [[Parsley]], finely chopped\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Boil]] the [[coditos]] for about 15 minutes or per packet instructions.\n| Rinse under cold water and drain thoroughly.\n| When the [[Pasta|pasta]] is cold, mix with the [[Tuna|tuna]], [[Cream|Cream]] and [[Mayonnaise|mayonnaise]] and place in the middle of a serving dish.\n| Arrange the [[Tomato|tomato]] slices around the [[Pasta|pasta]] and place the [[Olives|olives]] on top of it.\n| Sprinkle with the [[Hard boiled egg|hard boiled egg]]. and the [[Parsley|parsley]].\n}}\n===Variations===\n[[Coditos]] are not available in the UK, as far I can ascertain, although it may be found as elbow macaroni.  They are similar in shape to the [[Italian]] [[:Image:Pasta 2006 3.jpg|pipe pasta]] and this type can be used instead.\n[[Elicoidali]] is another fairly close equivalent that can be purchased directly from Waitrose.\n\nI already had some [[homemade garlic mayonnaise]], but had no idea how much would be made from 500 ml of olive oil, however,  3 good tablespoons of mayonnaise seemed just fine.  I also garnished the salad with a little [[smoked paprika]] to add a bit of extra interest.\nMany people like to use [[Cream|Cream]] in this salad because it reduces acidity in the dish due to the [[Mayonnaise|mayonnaise]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Ensalada de coditos]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Ensalada de coditos]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes|Ensalada de coditos]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes|Ensalada de coditos]]\n[[Category:Freshwater fish recipes|Ensalada de coditos]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Ensalada de coditos]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Pasta recipes|Ensalada de coditos]]\n[[Category:Pasta salad recipes|Ensalada de coditos]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes|Ensalada de coditos]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes|Ensalada de coditos]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Ensalada de coditos]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#ensaladadecoditos #coditos #tuna #cream #mayonnaise #tomatoes #pasta #egg #parsley #tomato #blackolives </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Ensalada de quinoa a la peruana",
                "revisions": [
                    {

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Ensalada de quinoa a la peruana Cooking with chillies recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#quinoa #vegetables #ensaladadequinoaalaperuana #diced #garlic #raisins #oliveoil #spanish #onion #unusualrecipes #salad \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Grown in the Andes quinoa is a grain that was beloved by the Incas. It can now be obtained in delicatessens and health food shops in the UK\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 613\n|PortionCalories = 102\n|DatePublished=25th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 25 minutes plus cooling time\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes \n |CookTime = 10 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Ensalsada de quinoa a la peruana recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Pretty, and Peruvian</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Another of Julia's winners</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nGrown in the Andes [[Quinoa|quinoa]] is a [[Grain|grain]] that was beloved by the Incas.  It can now be obtained in delicatessens and health food shops in the UK.  Supermarkets may well sell it too.  \n\n'''Please read carefully the article about [[Quinoa|quinoa]] before making this recipe.'''\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 340 g [[Quinoa|quinoa]]\n| 2 small [[Sweet peppers|sweet peppers]], one each of red and yellow\n| 3 [[Celery|celery]] sticks\n| 1-2 [[Green chillies|green chillies]], depending on size and strength\n| 1 large [[Spanish]] [[Onion|onion]]\n| 3 or more Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], according to size and taste\n}}\n: The above [[Vegetables|vegetables]] should be quite finely [[Diced|diced]] or chopped.\n* 50 ml [[Corn|corn]] or [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n* 1 tablespoon [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Take a pan of cold water and add the [[Quinoa|quinoa]].  \n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], then [[Simmer|simmer]] for around 10 minutes.\n| Drain and squeeze as much water as you can out of the [[Quinoa|quinoa]].\n| Once cool, mix in a bowl with the [[Vegetables|vegetables]].\n| Shake the [[Lemon|lemon]] and [[Oil|oil]] in a jar with a little seasoning and mix with the [[Salad|salad]].\n| Leave to chill for a short while.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nWill go with anything really, but I like to serve it as part of a collection of [[Salads|salads]], because the [[Quinoa|quinoa]] adds an extra texture.\n===Variations===\nYou can add any [[Vegetables|vegetables]], but try to keep it colourful,  Sometimes [[Raisins|raisins]] are included.\n===Chef's notes===\nThe easiest way, I find, to  squeeze the [[Quinoa|quinoa]] is to place it in either a [[jelly bag]] or [[butter muslin]] after draining.  Leave it for a while hanging over a bowl or sink and periodically squeeze the bag or muslin until you feel that you cannot extract any more water.\n--[[User:JuliaBalbilla|JuliaBalbilla]] 07:04, 14 January 2009 (UTC)\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Quinoa]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Quinoa]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Quinoa]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes|Quinoa]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Quinoa]]\n[[Category:Peruvian recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes|Quinoa]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Quinoa]]\n[[Category:Starters|Quinoa]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Quinoa]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Quinoa]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#quinoa #vegetables #ensaladadequinoaalaperuana #diced #garlic #raisins #oliveoil #spanish #onion #unusualrecipes #salad </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Ensalada de zanahorias (Carrot salad)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Ensalada de zanahorias (Carrot salad) a vegetarian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#carrots #salad #garlic #corianderleaves #jam #chile #lemonjuice \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This easy salad comes from Chile\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 352\n|PortionCalories = 88\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 4 minutes\n |PrepTime = 4 minutes\n |CookTime = None\n |Image = [[Image:Ensalada de zanahorias (Carrot salad) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Garlicy carrots!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Mmmm!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis easy [[Salad|salad]] comes from [[Chile]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 5 young [[Carrots|carrots]], peeled and grated\n| [[Garlic]] to taste, crushed\n| 60 ml [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]], finely chopped\n| Seasoning\n| 1 tablespoon [[Oil|oil]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put the [[Carrots|carrots]] in a serving bowl.\n| Place the remaining ingredients in an empty [[Jam|jam]] jar and shake vigorously until the ingredients have blended.\n| Pour the dressing over [[Carrots|carrots]] and give the [[Salad|salad]] a quick stir.\n| Serve chilled.\nInstead of garlic you can add grated ginger, it gives a very tangy flavour! [[Oven|oven]] 170\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Take the [[Chicken|chicken]] out of the [[Refrigerator|refrigerator]] about &#189; hour melted [[Butter|butter]].\n| Put the bird in the [[Oven|oven]] and [[Roast|roast]] it, [[Basting|basting]] from time to time with pan juices. [[Roast]] for about 20 minutes per pound, or until the internal temperature reaches 165F (75C).\n| Remove from [[Oven|oven]] and let stand for 15 minutes, loosely covered with [[Aluminium foil|aluminium foil]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nAn authentic accompaniment would be [[Caribbean corn bread]]\n===Recipe source===\n{{RecipeCourtesyOfCubanCuisine}}\n==See also==\n* '''[[Meat cooking time calculator Metric|A comprehensive guide to roast meat cooking times]]''' - give the time you want to carve your roast and we'll give you a timed step by step roasting guide\n* [[Jerk recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cuban recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:CubanCuisine.co.uk]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Marinaded]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #roast #marinade #fastandeasyjerkroastchicken #refrigerator #jerkrecipes #blend #sauce #aluminiumfoil #caribbeancornbread #brush </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Garlic fried chicken with a masa harina crust",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Garlic fried chicken with a masa harina crust recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #garlicfriedchickenwithamasaharinacrust #eggwhites #blackpepper #marinade #cornflour #refrigerate #cup #lemonjuice #masaharina #accompaniment \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=It is years since I deep-fried anything so this is almost new territory for me. Reading one of Ken Homs early cookbooks gave me the impetus to try\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1765\n|PortionCalories = 882\n|DatePublished=8th March 2015\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = An unusual accompaniment of garlic mushrooms and grilled tomatoes\n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  3 hours, 18 minutes\n|PrepTime =  3 hours, 10 minutes\n|CookTime =  8 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Garlic fried chicken with a masa harina crust.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Air frying is nicer</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">A few years ago this would have been great, but now I can get the same results using an air-fryer and a spray of olive oil.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\n\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\n\nIt is years since I [[deep-fried]] anything so this is almost new territory for me.  Reading one of Ken Hom's early cookbooks gave me the impetus to try it again.  I'm glad I did, it was really good and not at all greasy.\n\nThis is really an aide-memoir for me; next time I would add a tablespoon of [[Old India Taco Seasoning]] for a bit more [[Spice|spice]], and I would also hammer the [[Chicken|chicken]] flat before slicing up.  This would enable less [[Oil|oil]] to be used (not so wasteful), and it would also give a shorter, more uniform cooking time. As it was, we had to cook all of the chicken pieces a little longer to be sure the largest pieces were properly cooked.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 400g small [[Chicken|chicken]] fillets\n| 1 tablespoon [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Shaoxing rice wine|shaoxing rice wine]] [[Vinegar|vinegar]] - [[Balsamic vinegar|balsamic vinegar]] will be fine \n| 3 [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| A pinch of [[Salt|salt]] and [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| 2 [[Egg whites|egg whites]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Cornflour|cornflour]]\n| 1 [[Cup|cup]] [[Masa Harina|masa harina]]\n| 1 to 2 cups [[Sunflower oil|sunflower oil]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Cut the [[Chicken|chicken]] fillets into bite-sized pieces\n* Add to a [[Lock & Lock box]] together with the [[Crushed garlic|crushed garlic]], [[Rice|rice]] [[Wine vinegar|wine vinegar]], [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Black pepper|black pepper]].\n* Shake well to mix and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for an hour or more to allow the [[Marinade|marinade]] to penetrate the [[Meat|meat]].\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Garlic fried chicken with a masa harina crust frying.jpg|Frying in a wok\nImage:Chicken coated with masa.jpg|Coated with masa harina after the egg-white and cornflour stage\nImage:Garlic fried chicken marinading.jpg|Marinade for an hour or more\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Drain the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces in a [[Colander|colander]] and discard the [[Marinade|marinade]] juices.\n| Whisk the [[Egg whites|egg whites]] and [[Cornflour|cornflour]] in a bowl.\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces to the bowl and mix well. [[Refrigerate]] for 30 minutes.\n| Add the [[Cup|cup]] of [[Masa Harina|masa harina]] to a dry [[Lock and Lock box]], close the lid and shake hard to coat the [[Chicken|chicken]].\n| Heat a [[Wok|wok]] or [[Frying pan|frying pan]] with enough [[Oil|oil]] to just cover the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces.\n| Heat to 176\u00b0 C [350\u00b0 F] (a 2.5cm [1\"] cube of [[Bread|bread]] should [[Brown|brown]] in 60 seconds.\n| [[Fry]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces in 2 batches for about 4 minutes each batch.  Cut one of the largest pieces open to check that it is properly cooked.\n| Serve immediately.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n[[Chips]] and [[Salad|salad]] is probably the most usual [[Accompaniment|accompaniment]] for this.  We had this with an unusual, but fantastic combination; [[Stuffed mushrooms with garlic and Parmesan|garlic mushrooms]] and [[Grilled|grilled]] [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Deep fried]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #garlicfriedchickenwithamasaharinacrust #eggwhites #blackpepper #marinade #cornflour #refrigerate #cup #lemonjuice #masaharina #accompaniment </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Gorditas recipe",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Gorditas recipe Vegetarian, from Cookipedia.Co.Uk\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#masaharina #masa #tortilla #dough #yellowcornmeal #gorditas #bakingpowder #gorditasrecipe #vegetableoil #frying #flour \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A gordita in Mexican cuisine is a food which is characterised by a small, thick tortilla made with masa harina (processed corn flour)\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1225\n|PortionCalories = 204\n|DatePublished=31st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = 11 very lazily rolled gorditas\n |Servings = Serves 6 - Makes 11 to 12 [[Gorditas|gorditas]]\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 25 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 10 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Gorditas rolled.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Corn tortillas</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">These are lovely.  You must make them with Masa Harina, they won't be the same using normal cornmeal.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''A gordita''' in [[Mexican cuisine]] is a food which is characterised by a small, thick [[tortilla]] made with [[masa harina]] (processed corn flour). The gordita is in contrast to a [[taco]], which uses a thinner [[tortilla]]. \"Gordita\" means \"little fat one\" in Spanish. The gordita is typically baked on a comal, a small pan similar to a [[tava]].\n\nThe gordita's thick [[tortilla]] is typically split and filled with guisos (soups or stews) or casseroles, like [[chicken]], [[cochinita pibil]], [[nopales]], carne al pastor, etc. These are made mostly for lunch and are accompanied by many different types of [[salsas]]. The most traditional \"gordita\" in the central region of Mexico is filled with \"[[chicharr\u00f3n]] prensado\" (a type of stew made with pork rind and spices) and is called \"gordita de chicharr\u00f3n\".\nIn Durango, Mexico, gorditas are commonly made from wheat [[flour]] (harina de trigo) [[tortillas]] and look more like small [[pita breads]]. The [[dough]] (masa) is identical to that of the [[flour tortilla]]. It is cooked on a griddle (comal) with a hot piece of metal placed on top that resembles a clothes iron. The gordita fills up with steam and a small slit is cut into one side where it can be filled with guisados.\n\nThe best gorditas are made with [[Masa harina|masa harina]], though you can make them with [[Yellow cornmeal|yellow cornmeal]] if you cannot obtain [[Masa harina|masa harina]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 250g [[Masa harina|masa harina]] or fine [[Yellow cornmeal|yellow cornmeal]]\n| &#189; level teaspoon of [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 1 heaped teaspoon of [[Baking powder|baking powder]]\n| 350 ml very hot water\n| [[Yellow cornmeal]] for rolling\n| [[Vegetable oil]] for [[Frying|frying]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Masa|masa]] and [[Salt|salt]] to a large bowl and make a well in the centre.\n| Mix the [[Baking powder|baking powder]] into the hot water and pour into the centre of the [[Masa|masa]].\n| Using a spoon, fold the [[Masa|masa]] into the water, once it begins to combine, [[Kneading bread|knead]] with your hands until a firm malleable [[Dough|dough]] is produced.\n| Divide the [[Dough|dough]] into 12 balls, dust the work surface with cornmeal and roll each one out to about the size of a fried egg, leaving them quite thick.\n| Heat a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]] and add a few glugs of [[Oil|oil]]\n| Fill the pan with as many [[Gorditas|gorditas]] as will fit and [[Fry|fry]] for 3 minutes a side, turning once.  They are ready to eat once they have [[Puffed|puffed]] up a little.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nSlice them open like [[Pitta breads|pitta breads]] and fill with [[Mexican]] treats\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Prepared foods]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#masaharina #masa #tortilla #dough #yellowcornmeal #gorditas #bakingpowder #gorditasrecipe #vegetableoil #frying #flour </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
