[[Quesadillas|quesadillas]] using [[Philadelphia Light with Garlic and Herbs|philadelphia light with garlic and herbs]].\n\n{{PhiladelphiaPermission}}\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 large cooked [[Chicken breast|chicken breast]], thinly sliced\n| 3 tablespoons [[sweetcorn]]\n| 3 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], finely sliced\n| 1 dsp [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]]\n| 2 large [[Tortillas|tortillas]]\n| 50 g [[Philadelphia Light with Garlic & Herbs]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Heat [[Chicken|chicken]], [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]], [[Spring onion|spring onion]] and [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]] with 2 tablespoons of water in a small pan, stirring occasionally.\n| Spread one of the [[Tortillas|tortillas]] with the Philly. Spoon the [[Chicken|chicken]] mixture over one [[Tortilla|tortilla]] and top with the other.\n| Heat a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]] and add the filled [[Tortilla|tortilla]]. Cook for 2-3 minutes or until golden [[Brown|brown]].\n| Turn over with a large spatula and cook the other side until golden [[Brown|brown]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nSlice into 4 [[Wedges|wedges]] and serve with a [[Green salad|green salad]].\n===Recipe source===\n\n* [http://www.philadelphia.co.uk/philadelphia3/page?siteid=philadelphia3-prd&locale=uken1&PagecRef=609&rid=47 The Philadelphia recipe website]\n\n==See also ==\n{{OtherRecipes Philadelphia light with garlic and herbs}}\nWe have a number of tested recipes for '''Quesadillas''':\n* [[Cheese and ham quesadillas]]\n* [[Crab quesadillas]]\n* [[Hollywood Quesadillas]]\n* [[Sincronizada recipe|Sincronizada]] (explaining the difference between Sincronizadas & quesadillas)\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Ecuadorian recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Peruvian recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Philadelphia recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Cookery cheats]]\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#philadelphiachickenandsweetcornquesadillas #tortilla #tortillas #chicken #tomatopuree #sweetcorn #recipesfromothersites #sincronizadarecipe #springonions #greensalad #hollywoodquesadillas </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Picadillo",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Picadillo a beef recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#picadillo #beef #bellpepper #tomatoes #garlic #potato #vegetables #spanishrice #unusualrecipes #browning #diced \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Picadillo is a dish mainly consisting of ground beef typically found in Puerto Rico, Cuba, Mexico, and other Latin American countries\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2856\n|PortionCalories = 476\n|DatePublished=8th December 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 50 minutes\n|PrepTime = 10 minutes\n|CookTime = 40 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Picadillo recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Home cooking!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">We love this</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nPicadillo is a dish mainly consisting of ground [[Beef|beef]] typically found in Puerto Rico, Cuba, Mexico, and other Latin American countries. In Mexico and Puerto Rico it is sometimes used as a filling, such as for [[Tacos|tacos]], and can be mixed with [[Vegetables|vegetables]]. It can also be prepared as a type of stew. In most other Latin American countries it consists of a common table from where people pick small beef pieces or other food such as [[French fries|french fries]]. The name comes from the Spanish word, \"picar\" which means \"to mince\" or \"to chop\".\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500 g (1 lb 2 oz) of lean [[minced]] [[Beef|beef]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 4 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], chopped\n| 284 ml (&frac12; pint) [[Beef stock|beef stock]] \n| 1 large [[Green bell pepper|green bell pepper]],deseeded and chopped\n| 3 large russet [[Potato|potato]], cubed, bite size\n| 1 400 g (14.5 oz) tin [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] together with the juice\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Oil|oil]]\n| 1/8 teaspoon [[Sea salt|sea salt]] \n| 2 tablespoons of [[Tex-Mex seasoning]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a large, heavy pan, heat the [[Oil|oil]] to medium-high heat. Add the [[Onions|onions]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Bell pepper|bell pepper]] and seasoning to the pan.\n| When the [[Bell pepper|bell pepper]] starts to discolour, add to it ground [[Beef|beef]], stirring to break up large pieces and [[Brown|brown]] evenly, about 7 minutes. \n| As [[Meat|meat]] is [[Browning|browning]], add [[Potato|potato]], [[Beef|beef]] broth and [[Diced|diced]] [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]. \n| [[Simmer]] until the potato is cooked and the picadillo has thickened, stirring occasionally.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with [[Spanish rice]] and tortilla.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Cuban recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#picadillo #beef #bellpepper #tomatoes #garlic #potato #vegetables #spanishrice #unusualrecipes #browning #diced </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

title": "Platillo Moros y Cristianos",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Platillo Moros y Cristianos, Meat and bean recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#rice #beans #platillomorosycristianos #coconut #blackbeans #thyme #springonions #coriander #coconutmilk #pints #garlic \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=The \"Moors\" refer to the black beans, and \"Christians\" to the white rice - a reference to the early settlers of Cuba\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2459\n|PortionCalories = 614\n|DatePublished=3rd December 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4 to 6 people\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 13 hours 10 minutes\n |PrepTime = 12 hours 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour\n |Image = [[Image:Platillo Moros y Cristianos recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Probably not allowed now!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">In this PC crazy world, I expect this dish would have to be renamed now!  Nice meal though.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Platillo Moros y Cristianos''', ('''moors and christians''', '''moros''' or '''moro''') is the national dish of Cuba, their version of the [[Rice|rice]] and [[Beans|beans]] combination found throughout the Caribbean and in Brazil. It is also found in Puerto Rico and the Dominican Republic, and expatriate communities of each of these cultures. It was introduced during the Nicaraguan Sandinista regime when both countries mixed culturally because of strong ties. The dish also takes after the name '''gallo pinto''', used in Nicaragua and Costa Rica. \n[[Image:Gallo pinto.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Gallo pinto, 'painted rooster']]\n\nThe \"Moors\" refer to the [[Black beans|black beans]], and \"Christians\" to the white [[Rice|rice]] - a reference to the early settlers of Cuba for whom the Reconquista of Spain was a recent memory.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 600 g [[Rice|rice]]\n| 200 g [[Black beans|black beans]]\n| 3 sprigs [[Thyme|thyme]]\n| 2 tablespoons chopped [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and stems\n| 1 whole [[Coconut|coconut]], meat removed and finely grated.\n| A pinch of [[Salt|salt]]\n| 2 [[Cloves garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 3 [[Spring onions|spring onions]]\n| &frac14; teaspoon [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n| 2 [[Pints|pints]] hot water\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Soak [[Beans|beans]] overnight, rinse and drain thoroughly\n| Add two cups of the water the beans were soaked in to the [[Coconut|coconut]] and squeeze through a [[Sieve|sieve]]. Discard the coconut gratings.\n| Repeat this extraction of the [[Coconut|coconut]] until all of the water is used\n| Put [[Beans|beans]] and [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] in a pan with [[Garlic|garlic]].\n| Cook until the [[Beans|beans]] are tender, but not overcooked\n| Add [[Spring onions|spring onions]], [[Pepper|pepper]], [[Thyme|thyme]] and one tablespoon of the [[Coriander|coriander]]\n| [[Boil]] for 5 minutes, then add [[Rice|rice]] and [[Salt|salt]].  Boil until the rice is cooked, adding more water if required\n| Serve sprinkled with the remaining chopped [[Coriander|coriander]]\n}}\n===Variations===\nFor a non-vegetarian version of this dish, add some chopped shoulder of pork, at step 6, with the spring onions.\n\nWe have a [[Moros y Cristianos|Spanish version of Moros y Cristianos here]].\n\nA can of [[coconut milk]] could be used instead of processing a real coconut.\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Cuban recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rice #beans #platillomorosycristianos #coconut #blackbeans #thyme #springonions #coriander #coconutmilk #pints #garlic </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]

title": "Pollo con arroz (Chicken with Rice)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Pollo con arroz (Chicken with Rice) a meat recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #casserole #rice #garlic #chickenstock #onion #saffron #dicedchiliancho #artichokehearts #arrozconpollo #boil \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Throughout Latin America and the Caribbean, it is known as Arroz con pollo (Rice with chicken) but this Paraguayan version of the dish reverses the\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1212\n|PortionCalories = 202\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = 6 people\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 1 hour 30 minutes\n|PrepTime = 30 minutes\n|CookTime = 1 hour\n|Image = [[Image:Pollo con arroz (Chicken with Rice) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice, with rice</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Simple to make too</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\nThroughout Latin America and the Caribbean, it is known as [[Arroz con pollo]] (Rice with chicken) but this Paraguayan version of the dish reverses the ingredient names in the title.\n\nYou could reduce the amount of rice if making this for less than 6 people. Allow a maximum of 75g uncooked rice per person and double the volume of liquid to rice. Eg: 1 cup of rice to 2 cups of water or stock.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1.35-1.6kgs [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces \n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], finely chopped\n| 1 [[Sweet pepper|sweet pepper]] of any colour, seeded and chopped\n| 3 [[Tomatoes, peeled|tomatoes, peeled]] and chopped\n| Seasoning\n| 1 litre [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]]\n| Small pinch of [[Saffron|saffron]], crumbled\n| 400g long-grain [[Rice|rice]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| To remove the starch for the rice, rinse in a [[sieve]] under cold running water until it runs clear. Allow to drain.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a heavy [[Frying pan|frying pan]] and saut\u00e9 the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces until they are golden on both sides.\n| Transfer the [[Chicken|chicken]] to a flame-proof [[Casserole|casserole]].\n| In the [[Oil|oil]] remaining in the pan, saut\u00e9 the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] until they are soft.\n| Add to the [[Casserole|casserole]] with the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], seasoning, 425ml of the [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] and the [[Saffron|saffron]].\n| [[Simmer]], covered, over low heat for 30 minutes, turning the chicken pieces once to ensure they cook properly.\n| Add the remaining stock to the [[Casserole|casserole]], add the [[Rice|rice]] and the reserved solids, stir to mix and bring a [[Boil|boil]] over a fairly brisk heat.\n| Arrange the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces on top of the [[Rice|rice]].\n| Reduce the heat, cover, and cook over a very low heat until the rice is tender and all the liquid has been absorbed, about 20 minutes.\n| Serve directly from the caserole.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Pollo con arroz (Chicken with Rice) cooked.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Pollo con arroz, cooked\nImage:Pollo con arroz (Chicken with Rice) simmer.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Pollo con arroz, rice just in, ready to simmer\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nIf desired, [[Artichoke hearts|artichoke hearts]] may be scattered through the chicken\n===Chef's notes===\nI'm afraid I have to add [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[chili]] to most dishes.  This has been no exception.  I added 5 cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and chopped, 1 teaspoon of dried [[diced chilli pasilla]] & 1 teaspoon of dried [[diced chili ancho]].  I think it might have been a little bland without.\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken with rice]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Chicken with rice]]\n[[Category:Paraguayan recipes|Chicken with rice]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken with rice]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Chicken with rice]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Chicken with rice]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes|Chicken with rice]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #casserole #rice #garlic #chickenstock #onion #saffron #dicedchiliancho #artichokehearts #arrozconpollo #boil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

title": "Porotos granados (Bean and vegetable stew)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Porotos granados Bean and vegetable stew Cooking with chillies recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#garlic #squash #bean #fry #marrow #onions #paprika #simmer #beans #pumpkin #redchillies \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This vegetarian version of Chile's national dish comes strongly recommended by our Chilean visitor, Gabriela: \"You can't say you have lived if you've\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 634\n|PortionCalories = 158\n|DatePublished=19th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 2 hours 15 minutes plus overnight soak\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 2 hours\n |Image = [[Image:Porotos granados (Bean and vegetable stew) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice veggie curry / chilli</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I've lived!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\nThis [[Vegetarian|vegetarian]] version of [[Chile]]'s national dish comes strongly recommended by our Chilean visitor, [[User:Gabriela|Gabriela]]: \"''You can't say you have lived if you've never tried Porotos Granados.''\"\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 225 g [[Haricot beans|haricot beans]], soaked in cold water overnight\n| 3 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 2 medium [[Onions|onions]], finely chopped\n| [[Garlic]] to taste, peeled and crushed\n| 2 tablespoons sweet [[Paprika|paprika]]\n| [[Red chillies]], to taste, finely chopped\n| 225 g [[sweetcorn]]\n| 450 g [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]], [[Marrow|marrow]] or [[Squash|squash]], cut into 2.5 cm cubes\n| 450 g [[Tomatoes, peeled|tomatoes, peeled]] and roughly chopped or 1 x 400 g tin of chopped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Dried thyme|dried thyme]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Dried|dried]] [[Basil|basil]] - see [[Talk:Porotos granados (Bean and vegetable stew)|the discussion page]]\n| Seasoning to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Drain and rinse the [[Beans|beans]] and place in a large pan.\n| Cover with water, bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and boil vigorously for 10 minutes.\n| Reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 1-1&frac12; hours until tender.\n| Drain and set aside, reserving half of the [[Bean|bean]] liquid.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a large saucepan, add the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Fry|fry]] until soft.\n| Stir in the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Paprika|paprika]] and [[Fry|fry]] for a further 5 minutes.\n| Add the remaining ingredients and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 15 minutes to blend the flavours.\n| Add some [[Bean|bean]] liquid if necessary and continuing [[Simmering|simmering]] until the [[Marrow|marrow]] or [[Squash|squash]] has disintegrated.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe in large bowls with [[rice]] and/or [[tortillas]] and  [[Pebre chileno (Chilean hot pepper sauce)|pebre chileno]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Porotos granados (bean and vegetable stew)]]\n[[Category:Chilean recipes|Porotos granados (bean and vegetable stew)]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper Pupusas are hand-made and thick\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 489\n|PortionCalories = 61\n|DatePublished=27th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Cheese pupusa with curtido\n|Servings = Serves 8 - Will fill about 8 pupusa\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 2 hours 20 minutes\n|PrepTime = 2 hours\n|CookTime = 20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Cheese pupusa recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Hard work</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Lots of work for street food.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nA pupusa is a stuffed corn-tortilla, usually served with a spicy coleslaw called [[curtido]].\n\nPupusas are hand-made and thick. Like all [[corn tortillas]], they are made using [[masa harina]].  They originate from El Salvador. \n\nThis is not true to the original which uses pork rinds.  This slightly healthier version is stuffed with a bacon tomato and green pepper mixture\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 8 rashers [[bacon]]\n| 2 [[cloves garlic, crushed]]\n| 4 [[tomatoes]]\n| 1 [[green bell pepper]]\n| [[Ghee]] or [[olive oil]] for [[frying]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Fry the crushed [[Garlic|garlic]] for a minute in the hot ghee or oil\n| Fry the [[bacon]] until cooked, but not crisp\n| deseed and finely chop the [[green pepper]]\n| Grind or blend the [[bacon]] and [[tomatoes]] into a rough paste\n| Stir in the chopped [[peppers]]\n| [[Corn tortilla recipe|Make the tortillas as shown here]], but don't cook them yet\n| Divide the mixture into balls, slightly larger than golf-balls and place each ball in the centre of the tortilla and press the mixture out, leaving a gap around the edge\n| Cover with another tortilla and press together to seal\n| Heat a griddle pan or heavy frying pan and wipe over with a lightly oiled kitchen towel\n| Cook each  pupusa until it is nicely [[toasted]].  This will take about 4 minutes a side\n| Keep warm while you cook the remaining pupusas\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[curtido]]\n===Variations===\n\nMake the pupusas with a combination of this, [[refried beans]] and the filling for [[Cheese pupusas]]\n===Chef's notes===\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Starters|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#bacon #curtido #pupusadechicharron #tomatoes #toasted #masaharina #peppers #garlic #griddled #oliveoil #greenbellpepper </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

You don't want the mixture too wet.\n| Mix in the [[spring onions]]\n| Divide the mix into eight portions and roll up in the [[tortillas]]\n| Place in an oven proof dish\n| Pour the soup over the [[tortillas]] and gently move them around so the soup fills all the gaps\n| Sprinkle with the [[cheese]]\n| Bake for 30 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[sour cream]] and finely chopped [[chillies]]!\n===Variations===\nAny interesting soup will do.                         "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Refried beans recipe Cooking with chillies\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#beans #onion #bacon #butter #litres #fry #refriedbeansrecipe #pints #mash #potatoricer #refriedbeans \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Refried beans are the essential ingredient for Mexican and Tex-Mex dishes. They are ideal for freezing\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1875\n|PortionCalories = 468\n|DatePublished=17th March 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 14 hours\n|PrepTime = 12 hours\n|CookTime = 2 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Refried beans.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Better than El Paso</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Fresher and not at all cloying or gloopy (which the tinned stuff is!)</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\n[[Refried beans]] are the essential ingredient for [[:Category:Mexican recipes|Mexican]] and [[:Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Tex-Mex]] dishes.  They are ideal for [[freezing]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500g (1lb 2oz) [[dried]] [[pinto beans]]\n| 1.2 [[litres]] (2 [[pints]]) water\n| 1 large [[onion]], chopped\n| 250g (9oz) [[smoked]] streaky [[bacon]], finely chopped\n| 1 small [[fresh red chili]], deseeded and finely chopped\n| 2 tablespoons [[olive oil]]\n| knob of [[butter]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Soak the [[beans]] overnight in plenty of water.  Drain and re-rinse.\n| [[Boil]] the [[beans]] in 1.2 [[litres]] (2 [[pints]]) of water boil until tender. Reserve the cooking water.\n| In a large [[frying]] pan or [[wok]], heat the [[oil]] and [[butter]] and [[fry]] the the [[onion]] until soft.\n| Add the [[bacon]] and [[fry]] it until cooked, but not crispy.\n| [[Mash]] the [[beans]], a [[potato ricer]] or [[Potato masher|masher]] is good for this,  then mix them with the [[fried]] [[bacon]] and [[onion]].\n| Stir in a little of the reserved cooking water so the [[beans]] are the same consistency as [[double cream]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot as a [[side dish]] or as an ingredient in your recipe.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beans #onion #bacon #butter #litres #fry #refriedbeansrecipe #pints #mash #potatoricer #refriedbeans </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

            }

title": "Ropa vieja a la cubana (Cuban beef stew)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Ropa vieja a la cubana (Cuban beef stew) a beef recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#diced #beef #tomatoes #paprika #garlic #vegetables #bayleaves #searing #carrots #fry #onion \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Literally meaning 'old clothes', this stew is a spicier version of the Spanish dish of the same name\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3616\n|PortionCalories = 904\n|DatePublished=8th December 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 2 hours 20 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 2 hours\n |Image = [[Image:Ropa Vieja a la Cubana recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Love the colour of your vegetables!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Nice and spicy too.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Frying the vegetables.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Frying the vegetables]]\nLiterally meaning 'old clothes', this [[Stew|stew]] is a spicier version of the [[Spanish]] dish of the same name.  Traditionally, it was a way of using up leftover [[Beef|beef]], but this recipe explains how to make it from scratch.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 900 g lean [[Beef|beef]] in one piece\n| [[Oil]] for [[Searing|searing]]\n| 2 medium [[Onions|onions]], 1 cut into quarters and the other finely [[Diced|diced]]\n| 2 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| A large pinch each of [[Sugar|sugar]] and [[Salt|salt]] \n| 600 ml hot water or weak [[Beef stock|beef stock]]\n| 30 ml [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 5 Cloves [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Diced|diced]]\n| 2 large [[Green chillies|green chillies]] or 4 small ones, finely [[Diced|diced]]\n| 60 g [[Fresh ginger|fresh ginger]] root\n| 3 [[Sweet peppers|sweet peppers]], one each of green, yellow and red, finely [[Diced|diced]]\n| A large pinch of [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n| A pinch each of [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]], sweet [[Paprika|paprika]] and [[Dried|dried]] [[Oregano|oregano]] or [[Marjoram|marjoram]]\n| 4 ripe [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], peeled and chopped\n| 2 [[Carrots|carrots]], peeled and cut into thickish [[Julienne|julienne]] strips\n| 1 teaspoon [[Flour|flour]] (optional)\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Searing|searing]] [[Oil|oil]] in a deep pan to a high temperature and briefly seal the [[Beef|beef]] on both sides.\n| Remove the pan from the heat and reduce the temperature to low-medium.\n| Add the quartered [[Onion|onion]], [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]], [[Sugar|sugar]], [[Salt|salt]] and sufficient water to cover the [[Beef|beef]].  The  water must be hot or the beef will become tough.\n| Cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for about 1&frac12; hours (adding more water if necessary) or until the [[Meat|meat]] is tender.  \n| Remove the [[Meat|meat]] and put in a dish, pour the [[Stock|stock]] into a jug and allow both to cool on one side. \n| Meanwhile, add the remaining [[Oil|oil]] to the same pan and gently [[Fry|fry]] the [[Diced|diced]] [[Onion|onion]], [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Chillies|chillies]] and [[Garlic|garlic]], until the garlic and onion are golden.\n| Add the [[Ground pepper|ground pepper]], [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]], [[Paprika|paprika]] and [[Herbs|herbs]] and allow to [[Fry|fry]] for 30 seconds or so.\n| Add the sweet [[Pepper|peppers]], [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Carrots|carrots]] and allow the mixture to thicken.  You can add a little [[Flour|flour]] to help you if necessary.\n| When the [[Meat|meat]] is cool, cut it into thin strips with scissors and add to the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] with the reserved [[Stock|stock]].\n| Heat through and serve.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nThe simplest way of serving this would be with plain, [[Steamed|steamed]], long-[[Grain|grain]] [[Rice|rice]].\n\n===Variations===\nIf you wish to use leftover [[Beef|beef]], cut up the [[Meat|meat]] as above and just add it to the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] with some strongish [[Beef stock|beef stock]].\n\nYou can add other [[Spices|spices]] such as [[Allspice|allspice]], [[Cumin|cumin]] or [[Coriander|coriander]].  [[Capers]] are also quite popular in Cuban cuisine.\n\n===Chef's notes===\nI use unrolled topside, recommended by our butcher as being less likely to fall apart, but thickish [[Steak|steak]] would also be fine.\n\n[[Jalape\u00f1o chillies]] are the more usual variety for this dish, but fresh ones are not easily obtained in the UK.  I used [[serrano chillies]] but if you want, any sort will be fine so long as you adjust the quantity according to the heat or lack of it of your chosen [[chillies]].  De-seed them if you wish.\n\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Beef stew]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Beef stew]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes|Beef stew]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Beef stew]]\n[[Category:Cuban recipes|Beef stew]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Beef stew]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Beef stew]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#diced #beef #tomatoes #paprika #garlic #vegetables #bayleaves #searing #carrots #fry #onion </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

teaspoons sweet [[Paprika|paprika]]\n| 1 teaspoon  [[Flour|flour]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] in a pan and gently [[Fry|fry]] the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Onions|onions]] for about 5 minutes until golden.\n| Add the [[Chilli|chilli]] and the [[Carrot|carrot]] and cook for a further 3 minutes.\n| Add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Wine|wine]] and after 5 minutes, add the [[Olives|olives]], [[Stock|stock]], seasonings, [[Herbs|herbs]] and [[Paprika|paprika]].\n| Stir well and allow the [[Sauce|sauce]] to cook slowly for about 30-40 minutes.\n| 5 minutes before the end of the cooking time, add the [[Flour|flour]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nMakes a good [[Sauce|sauce]] for [[Pasta|pasta]].\n===Variations===\nYou can vary the amount of [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Chilli|chilli]] to your personal taste.\n===Chef's notes===\nAdd more [[Oil|oil]] if necessary.\n==See also==\n* [[Chilli sauce|Many other chilli sauce recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Salsa salu]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Salsa salu]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces|Salsa salu]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Salsa salu]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Salsa salu]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Salsa salu]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine|Salsa]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#salsasalu #chilli #oliveoil #onions #paprika #carrot #garlic #sauce #flour #pasta #spicytomatosauce </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

#annatto #rice #fat \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is a pork stew from Ecuador\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4190\n|PortionCalories = 698\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6 to 8\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 2 hours 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 2 hours 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Seco de chancho (Dry Pork) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Very South American!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Hot and spicy flavours </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is a [[Pork|pork]] [[Stew|stew]] from Ecuador.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 30ml [[Annatto|annatto]] [[Oil|oil]] or [[Lard|lard]]\n| 1.35kg lean [[Shoulder of pork|shoulder of pork]], cut into 5cm cubes\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], finely chopped\n| [[Garlic]] to taste, crushed\n| 1 large [[Tomato|tomato]], peeled, seeded and chopped\n| 1 [[Red pepper|red pepper]], seeded and roughly chopped\n| [[Chillies]] to taste, finely chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]], roughly chopped\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Dried oregano|dried oregano]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]]\n| Pinch [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 425ml [[Lager|lager]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] or [[Lard|lard]] in a heavy [[Frying pan|frying pan]].\n| Add the [[Pork|pork]] and lightly saut\u00e9.\n| Remove the [[Pork|pork]] to a flameproof [[Casserole|casserole]] or sauteuse.\n| Drain off all but 2 tablespoons of [[Fat|fat]] from the [[Frying pan|frying pan]] and add the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]].\n| Saut\u00e9 until the [[Onion|onion]] is soft.\n| Add the [[Tomato|tomato]], [[Red pepper|red pepper]], [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Coriander|coriander]], [[Cumin|cumin]] and [[Oregano|oregano]] and [[Simmer|simmer]]  for about 10 minutes.\n| Season to taste and add the [[Sugar|sugar]].\n| Pour this mixture over the [[Pork|pork]] and add the [[Beer|beer]].\n| Cover and cook over a very low heat until the [[Pork|pork]] is tender, about 2 hours.\n| The [[Sauce|sauce]] should be quite thick, but if it is too watery, partially uncover during the second hour of cooking.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Rice|rice]].\n===Chef's notes===\nFollow the [[RSPCA Think Pig Checklist]] to make sure that your [[Pork|pork]] has come from pigs that have been reared to higher welfare standards.\n* http://bit.ly/rspcathinkpig\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Pork dry]]\n[[Category:Ecuadorian recipes|Pork dry]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Pork title": "Sincronizada recipe",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Sincronizada recipe Cheese, from Cookipedia.Co.Uk\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#cheese #ham #quesadillas #tortillas #sincronizadarecipe #flourtortillas #tortilla #sandwich #grilled #masa #cheddar \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=In Mexican cuisine, the sincronizada is a tortilla-based sandwich\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2455\n|PortionCalories = 1227\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 2\n |Difficulty = 1\n |ImageComment = A \"sincronizada\", cut into wedges\n |TotalTime = 25 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Sincronizada recipe recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Cheese tortilla sandwich</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I like mine with extra chillies!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\nIn [[Mexican Cuisine|Mexican cuisine]], the sincronizada is a [[Tortilla|tortilla]]-based [[Sandwich|sandwich]]. They are frequently confused with [[Quesadillas|quesadillas]], due to their resemblance to \"quesadillas\" sold in the United States. (U.S. quesadillas are usually made with [[Flour tortillas|flour tortillas]] rather than molded from [[Masa|masa]] in the [[Mexican]] style).\n\nSincronizadas (so called because the top and bottom [[Tortilla|tortilla]] are \"synchronized\" together) [[Sandwich|sandwich]] ingredients between two [[Tortillas|tortillas]]. The sandwich is then [[Grilled|grilled]].\n\n=== The difference between Sincronizadas & [[quesadillas]] ===\n''This is only a rough guide, there are many, many regional differences.''\n* Sincronizadas usually include [[Ham|ham]]\n* Sincronizadas are usually made with [[Wheat flour|wheat flour]] [[tortillas]]\n* Sincronizadas are usually served flat, cut into segments\n* [[Quesadillas]] are usually made with [[corn tortillas]], though can be made with [[flour tortillas]]\n* As well as [[cheese]], [[Quesadillas]] can often contain, meat, [[refried beans]] and vegetables.\n* [[Quesadillas]] are often rolled before serving.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 soft [[Flour tortillas|flour tortillas]]\n| 1 cup [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheese|cheese]].\n| 70g strong [[Cheddar]]. ''Original recipes suggest [[Oaxaca cheese]] or [[Monterey Jack cheese]]''.\n| 4 slices of thinly sliced [[Ham|ham]] or [[Prosciutto|prosciutto]], cut into strips\n| 2 red [[Hot chillies|hot chillies]], de-seeded and thinly sliced (or to taste)\n|* You can use [[Chilli|chilli]] [[Sauce|sauce]] instead if you prefer\n| A few thinly cut slices of fresh [[Tomato|tomato]]\n| A few rings of thinly sliced [[Onions|onions]]\n| A handful of [[Coriander|coriander]] or [[Parsley leaves|parsley leaves]], chopped finely\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Lay two of the [[Tortillas|tortillas]] side-by-side on a flat surface and sprinkle with half of the [[Cheese|cheese]]\n| Layer the half of [[Ham|ham]] on to the [[Cheese|cheese]]\n| Distribute the remaining ingredients apart from the [[Cheese|cheese]] and [[Ham|ham]]\n| Top with the remaining [[Ham|ham]] and [[Cheese|cheese]]\n| Complete the 'sandwiches' by covering with the [[Tortillas|tortillas]]\n| On a [[Griddle|griddle]] or a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]], cook the sincronizadas, one at-a-time until the [[Tortillas|tortillas]] are lightly [[Browned|browned]] and starting to become crispy, turning once\n| Cut each sincronizada into 6 quadrants\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot with [[Guacamole|guacamole]] and a [[Green salad|green salad]]\n===Variations===\nChange the [[Cheddar cheese]] for a Mexican type of cheese that is called [[Oaxaca cheese|\"quesillo/queso oaxaca\"]] which can be easily torn into thinner strands and melts faster. \n\nI usually put some mayonnaise on the tortillas then the ham,cheese, a bit of fried beans, and cover it with the other tortilla with mayonnaise and another slice of ham. -- [[User:Pepekike]] 04:28, 21 July 2011 \n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n* [[Talk:Sincronizada_recipe|Visitor comments]] relating to this recipe\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cheese #ham #quesadillas #tortillas #sincronizadarecipe #flourtortillas #tortilla #sandwich #grilled #masa #cheddar </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "So'o-yosopy",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=So'o-yosopy a cheese recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#sooyosopy #onions #rice #parmesancheese #onion #beef #tomato #tomatoes #driedoregano #cassava #grated \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=So'o-yosopy is the Guarani for 'Sopa de Carne' which is a beef stew from Paraguay. Guarani is one of the official languages there\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3905\n|PortionCalories = 650\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime =  25 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:So'o-yosopy recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Beef AND parmesan!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Yum!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nSo'o-yosopy is the Guarani for 'Sopa de Carne' which is a [[Beef|beef]] [[Stew|stew]] from Paraguay.  Guarani is one of the official languages there.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 900g lean sirloin or topside which has been [[Minced|minced]] twice.\n| 30ml [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 2 medium [[Onions|onions]], finely chopped\n| 1 sweet [[Green pepper|green pepper]] or 2 [[Hot chillies|hot chillies]], seeded and finely chopped\n| 1 tin of chopped [[tomatoes]]\n| 1.85 [[Litres|litres]] unsalted [[Beef Stock|beef stock]] or water\n| 115g [[Rice|rice]] or vermicelli\n| [[Salt]]\n| 20g [[Parmesan cheese]], [[Grated|grated]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Pulverise the [[Minced meat|minced meat]] in a [[Food processor|food processor]] and set aside including any juices.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] and saut\u00e9 the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] or [[Chillies|chillies]] until the [[onions]] are softened.\n| Add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and cook until the mixture is thick and well blended, about 5 minutes.\n| Cool the mixture slightly.\n| Put the [[Beef|beef]] and its juices into a saucepan.\n| Stir in the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Tomato|tomato]] mixture and add the unsalted [[Stock|stock]] or water, mixing well.\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] over a moderate heat, stirring with a wooden spoon.\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] or vermicelli and [[Simmer|simmer]], still stirring, until tender for about 15 minutes.\n| At this stage, and only at this stage, season.  If you do this before, the [[Meat|meat]] may separate from the liquid.\n| Cook for a few more minutes, stirring constantly and serve in bowls, garnished with the [[Parmesan cheese]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a [[Baked|baked]] [[Sweet potato|sweet potato]] or [[Boiled|boiled]] [[Cassava|cassava]] and some [[Bread|bread]] or [[Sopa paraguaya]].\n===Variations===\nOmit the [[Rice|rice]] or vermicelli and add 2 thinly sliced [[Carrots|carrots]] to the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Tomato|tomato]] mixture with a teaspoon of [[Dried oregano|dried oregano]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Beef soup]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Beef soup]]\n[[Category:Paraguayan recipes|Beef soup]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes|Beef soup]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes|Beef soup]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes|Beef soup]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Beef soup]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#sooyosopy #onions #rice #parmesancheese #onion #beef #tomato #tomatoes #driedoregano #cassava #grated </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

title": "Sopa paraguaya",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Sopa paraguaya a cheese recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#cornmeal #onions #butter #sopaparaguaya #cheese #cottagecheese #cheddarcheese #accompaniment #baking #sweetcorn #bread \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Although this literally means 'Paraguayan soup', this is in fact a type of bread made with cornmeal and cheese\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4220\n|PortionCalories = 527\n|DatePublished=4th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Servings: 8 - Makes enough for 8 people as a [[starter]] or [[accompaniment]]\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 45 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Sopa paraguaya recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Yay! Cheesy cornbread</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I love stuff like this - thanks Julia!</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nAlthough this literally means 'Paraguayan [[Soup|soup]]', this is in fact a type of [[Bread|bread]] made with [[Cornmeal|cornmeal]] and [[Cheese|cheese]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 115g [[Butter|butter]]\n| 2 medium [[Onions|onions]], finely chopped\n| 225g [[Cottage cheese|cottage cheese]]\n| 225g [[Cheddar cheese]], [[Grated|grated]]\n| 225g [[Cornmeal|cornmeal]]\n| 340g [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]], pulverised\n| 1 teaspoon [[Coarse salt|coarse salt]]\n| 280ml [[Milk|milk]]\n| 6 [[Eggs|eggs]] separated\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6), [fan oven 180\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Grease a [[Baking|baking]] tin measuring about 25cm x 32cm.\n| Heat half of the [[Butter|butter]] and saut\u00e9 the [[Onions|onions]] until they are softened and set aside.\n| [[Cream]] the remaining [[Butter|butter]] and add to the [[Cottage cheese|cottage cheese]], blending thoroughly.\n| Add the [[Cheddar cheese]] and the [[Onions|onions]].\n| In another bowl combine the [[Cornmeal|cornmeal]], [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Milk|milk]] and mix thoroughly.\n| Combine the [[Corn|corn]] mixture with the [[Cheese|cheese]] mixture, blending thoroughly.\n| Beat the [[Egg white|egg white]] until they form soft peaks and beat the [[Yolks|yolks]] separately.\n| Combine the two and fold them into the [[Cornmeal|cornmeal]] and [[Cheese|cheese]] mixture.\n| Pour the [[Batter|batter]] into the [[Baking|baking]] tin and [[Bake|bake]] for about 45 minutes.\n| Whilst still warm, cut the bread into squares and allow to cool on a wire rack.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe on its own, or with [[Meat|meat]] and [[Poultry dishes|poultry dishes]].  It is the traditional [[Accompaniment|accompaniment]] to [[So'o-yosopy]].\n===Variations===\nYou can add a further 60g finely cubed [[Cheddar]] into the mixture at the last moment to give the [[Bread|bread]] a lightly different texture.  You could also use [[Parmesan]] if you want a cheesier flavour.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Paraguayan recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cornmeal #onions #butter #sopaparaguaya #cheese #cottagecheese #cheddarcheese #accompaniment #baking #sweetcorn #bread </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
}

title": "Wahaca - Mexican Market Eating - UK Restaurant chain",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Wahaca - Mexican Market Eating - Uk Restaurant chain - Cookipedia review\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#wahacamexicanmarketeatingukrestaurantchain #tacos #suppliers #wahacachillisauces #hotsauces #latinamericanrecipes #blackbeans #blackbean #taquitos #quesadilla \n|hashtagrev=12032020\n|description=My review of the fantastic Wahaca, Mexican Market Eating chain after a recent visit to the Covent Garden Restaurant\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n__NOTOC__\n==Wahaca - Mexican Market Eating - UK Restaurant chain==\nI love Mexican food and I think this is the best British Mexican restaurant chain I've been to in a very long while.  If the name already rings a bell, it's probably because you've seen Wahaca's co-founder, Cheltenham born Thomasina Miers on Channel 5's ''Mexican Food Made Simple'' tv cookery program or maybe you remember her as BBC 2's 2005 ''Masterchef'' winner.\n\nWe popped in for a light early evening meal and were instantly impressed.  It has the ''cool'' buzz that I remember from Bob Payton's ''Chicago Pizza Pie Factory'' way back in the 80's.  When we left it even had the matching hoards of people queuing down the stairs to get a table.\n\nFor under \u00a320 we had the Wahaca Street Food Selection for 2 people: 3 pork pibil [[tacos]], 3 winter vegetable [[tacos]], 1 large huitlacoche [[quesadilla]], 2 [[black bean]] tostadas and 2 chicken [[taquitos]] with green rice & [[black beans]].  My favourite way to eat, lots of little portions of different flavoured dishes, which you can eat with your fingers. Unlike some British Mexican restaurant offerings that appear to come straight from the microwave or the deep fat frier, these were cooked to order and packed with fresh vegetables.  Oh and don't forget the mandatory selection of [[hot sauces]] on your table. \n<gallery widths=250px perrow=5>\nImage:Wahaca Covent garden 4.jpg|Facia - Wahaca, 66 Chandos St, Covent Garden, London WC2N 4HG\nImage:Wahaca Covent garden 3.jpg|Lobby / Reception area Wahaca Covent Garden\nImage:Wahaca Mexican Mobile Eating.jpg|The Wahaca Mexican Mobile Eating van, under the trees, Canada Square Park\nImage:Wahaca Covent garden 1.jpg|So light and airy, you would never know you were in the a basement\nImage:Wahaca book of matches - Serrano chilli seeds.jpg|Not a book of matches, the complimentary packet of Serrano chilli seeds we were given as we left!\nImage:Wahaca The South Bank Experiment.jpg|The South Bank Experiment<br />Built from 8 recycled shipping containers!\n</gallery>\nThe decor was cleverly done, it was only as we left, I remembered we had actually been in a windowless basement.  The service was impeccable and everyone was was extremely helpful.  A very slick operation that has been replicated in 11 locations in the South East, 13 if you count the 2 Mexican Mobile Eating vans. Congratulations Tommi, I'm already planning another excuse to get back into London for another Mexican feast!\n\n''Update:'' In the short time since this article was written, we've been to even more Wahaca locations, every time the food and service has been exemplary.  Our last visit, to the South bank Experiment, deserves a special mention.  The restaurant overlooks the river, being situated on a the first floor terrace of the 1950's minimalist building, The Queen Elizabeth Hall, which sits between The Royal Festival Hall and The Hayward Gallery. The 'South Bank Experiment' is so named because of the restaurants unique construction materials. 8 recycled shipping containers!  Now that's what I call recycling.  It also affords wonderful views of the river and should you want to eat on the move, the mobile eating truck is at river level in front of the restaurant.\n\n===Geographic Locations===\n: '''Wahaca [[Lard]] could be used without any problems but the recipe would no longer be vegetarian.\n===Chef's note===\nIf you don't have a [[tortilla press]], use 2 chopping boards or just two sheets of wood as a substitute. Although it's a Mexican dish, it would work in place of any rice dish.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 200g (7 oz) [[long grain rice]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[vegetable oil]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[ground achiote seeds]] ([[annatto powder]])\n| 1 small [[onion]], finely chopped\n| 2 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, crushed\n| 475 ml (16 fl oz) good [[vegetable stock|vegetable]] or [[chicken stock]]\n| 50 g (2 oz) pickled [[jalepeno chili slices]]\n| sea [[salt]]\n| Fresh [[coriander leaves]], chopped\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a sieve, rinse the [[rice]] for a few minutes under cold running water  to remove excess starch.  The water should run clear once done\n| Heat the oil in a pan and fry the [[onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] for 4 minutes until soft and translucent\n| Add the [[annatto powder]] and fry for a further 3 minutes\n| Mix the rice into the [[onion]] mix and stir well to coat all of the rice\n| Add the stock, bring to the boil and [[simmer]], covered, for 25 minutes or until the rice has absorbed all of the liquid.  A sheet or so of [[tin-foil]] under the pan lid helps to make a good seal\n| Add extra water if the [[rice]] dries out before it's cooked\n| Add the chopped [[chillies]] and add [[salt]] to taste\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe in a large bowl, garnished with [[coriander]] leaves\n\n===Variations===\n\nServe cold as a salad.\n\nIf you don't want to add [[chillies]], try some sliced [[roasted red peppers]] instead.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Rice]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#annattopowder #rice #onion #garlic #chillies #roastedredpeppers #vegetableoil #longgrainrice #chickenstock #achioteseeds #groundachioteseeds </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Yellow rice - Mexican a vegetarian chili recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#onion #annattopowder #rice #chillies #garlic #vegetablestock #simmer #roastedredpeppers #longgrainrice #boiledorsimmered #coriander \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=An unusual rice dish that uses ground achiote seeds annatto powder to colour it\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 796\n|PortionCalories = 132\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 45 minutes \n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 35 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Yellow rice (Mexican) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice rice Man!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">And colourful too.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Yellow rice (Mexican) ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Yellow rice - The ingredients]]\nAn unusual [[rice]] dish that uses ground [[achiote seeds]] ([[annatto powder]]) to colour it.  Although it's a Mexican dish, it would work in place of any rice dish.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 200g (7 oz) [[long grain rice]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[vegetable oil]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[ground achiote seeds]] ([[annatto powder]])\n| 1 small [[onion]], finely chopped\n| 2 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, crushed\n| 475 ml (16 fl oz) good [[vegetable stock]]\n| 50 g (2 oz) pickled [[jalepeno chili slices]]\n| sea [[salt]]\n| Fresh [[coriander leaves]], chopped\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a sieve, rinse the [[rice]] for a few minutes under cold running water  to remove excess starch.  The water should run clear once done\n| Heat the oil in a pan and fry the [[onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] for 4 minutes until soft and translucent\n| Add the [[annatto powder]] and fry for a further 3 minutes\n| Mix the rice into the [[onion]] mix and stir well to coat all of the rice\n| Add the stock, bring to the boil and [[simmer]], covered, for 25 minutes or until the rice has absorbed all of the liquid.  A sheet or so of [[tin-foil]] under the pan lid helps to make a good seal\n| Add extra water if the [[rice]] dries out before it's cooked\n| Add the chopped [[chillies]] and add [[salt]] to taste\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe in a large bowl, garnished with [[coriander]] leaves\n===Variations===\nServe cold as a salad.\n\nIf you don't want to add [[chillies]], try some sliced [[roasted red peppers]] instead.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Rice]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#onion #annattopowder #rice #chillies #garlic #vegetablestock #simmer #roastedredpeppers #longgrainrice #boiledorsimmered #coriander </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
